Compliance with All Employee -Related Laws 
and Regulations  
Our aim with the legal overview is to alert you to your obligations as a 
Canadian employer. The following references highlight a cross section of 
relevant employment rules and regulations for Franchisees to comply with. 
This overview is not inclusive of every law applicable to your business. It is 
the Franchise es responsibility to verify all laws, rules, and regulations that 
apply in their province, territory, regional district, and municipality where 
they are operating their business(es) as well as any changes and updates. 
Please consult with your attorney or h uman resource professional for 
guidance on all employment -related laws that apply to your franchised 
business.  
The Canada Labour Code  
Generally, the Canada Labour Code covers:  
‚Ä¢ Employment standards, including general holidays, annual vacations, 
working hours, unjust dismissals, minimum wage, layoff procedures, 
and severance pay  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -9 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  ‚Ä¢ Workplace health and safety  
‚Ä¢ Industrial relations ‚Äî certification of unions, labour -management 
relations, collective bargaining, and unfair labour practices  
See a full list of the federally regulated sectors covered by the Canada 
Labour Code. Most other occupations are covered under provincial and 
territorial laws. Every province or territory has an office that deals with 
labour and employment laws, which can provide information about fair pay, 
hours of work, rest periods, and working conditions.  
Part III of the  Canada Labour Code  discusses federal labour standards. 
These standards set out the employment conditions for hours of work, 
payment of wages, leaves, vacation, holidays, and more. Federal labour 
standards apply to employees working in feder ally regulated businesses.  
Minimum Wage Requirements  
Franchisees must comply with provincial minimum wage regulations, which 
vary by province. Franchisees must monitor and implement rate changes as 
they occur, typically annually or semi -annually depending on the province.  
Statutory Holiday Pay  
Franchisees must observe statutory holidays with appropriate compensation. 
When employees work on statutory holidays, they are typically entitled to 
1.5 times their regular wage rate for each hour worked. The main federal 
statutory holidays include:  
‚Ä¢ New Year's Day  
‚Ä¢ Good Friday  
‚Ä¢ Canada Day  
‚Ä¢ Labour Day  
‚Ä¢ National Day for Truth and Reconciliation  
‚Ä¢ Christmas Day  
Minimum Wage Database  
There is additional information regarding minimum wages at minwage -
salairemin.service.canada.ca/en/index.html  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -10 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Standard Working Hours  
The standard Canadian workweek follows a consistent structure across most 
provinces. Employees typically work between 37.5 to 40 hours per week . 
Employers must ensure that employees do not exceed 48 hours in a 
workweek without proper authorization  
Recognizing that each location 's hours of operatio n must comply with both 
the landlord 's requirements and Franchisor requirements , Corporate will 
work with Franchisee s to determine the approved hours of operation  for 
each lo cation . 
Overtime Compensation  
Overtime regulations require careful attention from employers. The standard 
overtime threshold varies by province, but generally, overtime pay must be 
at least 1.5 times the employee's regular wage rate when employees work 
beyond:  
‚Ä¢ Eight hours in a day  
‚Ä¢ 40 hours in a week (some provinces ' threshold is 44 hours)  
Rest Periods and Breaks  
Proper break scheduling is essential for compliance and employee well -
being. Employers must provide:  
‚Ä¢ One 30 -minute meal break for every five consecutive hours of work  
‚Ä¢ A minimum of 24 hours' written notice when changing an employee's 
shift 
‚Ä¢ At least eight hours of rest between shifts  
Flexible Work Arrangements  
The Canada Labour Code provides rights and protections to help employees 
balance work and home life in conjunction with their employment. Any 
flexible arrangement cannot violate provincial provisions on hours, breaks, 
or rest periods.  Consult your human resources professional about  how this 
may apply to your location.  
 
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -11 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Canadian Legal Protected Leave Regulations  
Canadian employment law provides a comprehensive framework of 
protected leaves that ensures  employees can address critical life events 
without fear of job loss. The Canada Labour Code establishes minimum 
requirements for various types of leaves across federally regulated 
workplaces. Franchisees should recognize that leave provisions are designed  
to support work -life balance, address critical personal and family needs, and 
create a more compassionate and flexible workplace environment.  Each 
province has dist inct rules for maternity/parental, personal emergency, 
bereavement, sick leave etc.  
Work with your human resources professional or attorney to understand 
your obligation to your employees regarding:  
‚Ä¢ Medical and Illness Leave  
‚Ä¢ Parental and Family Leaves  
‚Ä¢ Family Caregiver and Medical Support Leaves  
‚Ä¢ Domestic and Sexual Violence Leave  
‚Ä¢ Personal and Sick Leave  
Different provinces may have variations in leave requirements, but most 
follow similar principles. Employers are generally not required to pay wages 
during a leave but must provide time off and job protection. Key 
considerations include:  
‚Ä¢ Minimum employment periods for leave eligibility  
‚Ä¢ Job protection during leave  
‚Ä¢ Potential benefits through Employment Insurance  
‚Ä¢ Notification requirements  
It is important to understand that granting employee leave is integral to 
creating an accommodating, compliant, and supportive work environment.  
Termination of Employment  
The Canada Labour Code outlines the necessary steps to follow when 
terminating an employment, including layoffs, and group terminations.  
Termination entitlements (notice pay, severance pay) are governed by 
provincial legislation and potentially common law. Review the application of 
this law with your human resources consultant.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -12 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Labour Standards for Interns  
Paid and unpaid intern rules differ by province. Interns are to be treated the 
same way as employees for the purposes of Part III of the Canada Labour 
Code. Employers must provide full labour standards protection to interns, 
and certain protection to student interns.  
Anti-discrimination and Anti -harassment Law Overview  
Understanding and implementing proper discrimination policies is crucial as 
Franchisees must create and maintain a workplace that is free from 
discrimination. It is important to note that there are different federal and 
provincial legislation requirements that Franchisees must be compliant with:  
‚Ä¢ Federal legislation through the Canadian Human Rights Act  
‚Ä¢ Provincial human rights codes.  
Franchisees must comply with both sets of laws, with the stricter standard 
always taking precedence.  
These laws protect individuals from discrimination based on characteristics 
including race, colo ur, national, or ethnic origin, religion, age, sex, sexual 
orientation, gender identity, or expression, marital status, family status, 
disability, genetic characteristics, and pardoned criminal convictions.  
Hiring Practices  
The Franchisee 's primary responsibility is to ensure equal treatment in all 
aspects of employment. This begins with hiring practices. Job postings and 
recruitment processes must be free from discriminatory language or 
requirements. All hiring decisions should be based solely on merit, 
qualifications, and the candidate's ability to perform essential job duties. 
Always maintain consistent screening and int erview procedures across all 
candidates to demonstrate fair treatment.  
Duty to Accommodate  
Employers must follow the duty to accommodate employees up to the point 
of undue hardship. Each province 's human rights code sets out the 
requirements. Reasonable adjustments to workplace conditions, schedules, 
or equipment to accommodate employees' needs related to protected 
grounds must be implemented.  
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -13 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  For example, work schedules may need to be modified for religious 
observances, workstations could be adapted for employees with disabilities, 
and flexible arrangements may be needed for family responsibilities. 
Document all accommodation requests and respo nses.  
Equal Pay  
Equal pay for equal work is a fundamental employer/employee requirement. 
Compensation systems must ensure that employees performing substantially 
similar work receive equal pay, regardless of their gender or other protected 
characteristics. This applies to  all forms of compensation, including base 
salary, overtime rates, benefits, and bonuses. Regular audits of pay 
practices can help identify and correct any disparities.  
Employment Laws for Canadians with Disabilities  
Workplace accessibility is not just a legal requirement but a fundamental 
aspect of creating an inclusive and equitable work environment. The aim is 
to remove barriers and create opportunities that allow all individuals to 
contribute fully to the workplace , regardless of their abilities.  In addition to 
the Accessible Canada Act, provincial accessibility standards or disability 
legislation also apply (e.g., Accessibility for Ontarians with Disability Act). 
You must ensure compliance with both federal and pro vincial requirements.  
Legal Protections and Rights  
Canadian employment law provides comprehensive protection for individuals 
with disabilities. The Canadian Human Rights Act of 1985 seeks to prevent 
discrimination and improve access to employment, services, and facilities 
across all sectors.  
This legislation ensures that people with disabilities have equal opportunities 
in the workplace, prohibiting discrimination based on physical or mental 
disability in federal workplaces and federally regulated industries.  
Hiring and Recruitment Protections  
Employers must follow strict guidelines during the hiring process. Job 
candidates are not required to disclose disability status, and employers are 
prohibited from asking discriminatory questions. The focus must remain on 
the candidate's ability to perform essential job functions with reasonable 
workplace accommodations.  You must verify that any healthcare 
professional holds valid provincial licensure before hiring. The scope -of-
practice rules differ across provinces.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -14 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Duty to Accommodate  
Employers have a legal obligation to accommodate employees with 
disabilities to the point of "undue hardship." This means making meaningful 
changes to work environments, rules, standards, and policies to enable 
employees with disabilities to perform the es sential duties of their job.  
Accommodations can take various forms, including:  
‚Ä¢ Modifying work schedules  
‚Ä¢ Providing assistive technologies  
‚Ä¢ Adjusting physical workspace layouts  
‚Ä¢ Offering alternative communication methods  
‚Ä¢ Implementing flexible work arrangements  
‚Ä¢ Providing additional training or support  
Accommodation Process  
The accommodation process is collaborative and individualized. Employers 
must work with employees to understand their specific needs to streamline 
workplace accommodations. Workplace accommodations should be based on 
the current functional abilities of the worker, addressing both phys ical and 
cognitive requirements.  
The Accessible Canada Act  
The Accessible Canada Act (ACA) represents a significant shift in how 
Canadian businesses approach accessibility. The Act primarily affects 
federally regulated organizations.  
This includes banks, telecommunications companies, transportation 
providers (including railways, airlines, and bus companies), mining 
operations, and other businesses under federal jurisdiction.  
The size of your organization determines your specific obligations. For 
businesses with 100 or more employees, there's a requirement to publish 
detailed accessibility plans. Smaller federally regulated businesses with 99 
employees or less are currently exe mpted from some of these requirements, 
though they must still work to remove accessibility barriers.  
 
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -15 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  To meet the Act's requirements, businesses must take several concrete 
steps. This includes consulting with people with disabilities, developing and 
publishing accessibility plans, and creating processes for receiving and 
addressing feedback. The goal is to  identify, remove, and prevent barriers in 
areas like employment, physical spaces, and information technologies. There 
are enforcement and penalties for non -compliance.  
The Employment Equity Act  
The Employment Equity Act  is a federal law that requires federally regulated 
organizations and businesses to provide equal employment opportunities to 
four designated groups:  
‚Ä¢ Women  
‚Ä¢ Aboriginal peoples (Indian, Inuit, or M√©tis)  
‚Ä¢ People with disabilities  
‚Ä¢ Members of visible minorities  
The Legislated Employment Equity Program  
The Legislated Employment Equity Program  (LEEP) requires federally 
regulated organizations and businesses to report each year on how many 
individuals from the four designated groups are represented in their 
workplaces. They also have to show the steps they  have taken to achieve 
full representation.  
The goal of  LEEP is to ensure that employers that fall under the jurisdiction 
of the federal government reflect the composition of the general labour force 
in Canada. These federally regulated employers include approximately 500 
private -sector employers, 3 0 Crown corporations, and five other federal 
organizations with a combined workforce of over 760,000 employees.  
The Labour Program administers and enforces  LEEP, which is made 
mandatory under the provisions of the  Employment Equity Act.  
The Workplace Equity Information Management System  
The Workplace Equity Information Management System  (WEIMS) is an 
online application intended to be used by employers under the LEEP and 
federal contractors under the FCP.  
The WEIMS application helps employers meet their obligations under 
the Employment Equity Act, and federal contractors under the  FCP. 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -16 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Workers' Compensation Benefits  
Workers' compensation in Canada is a provincially managed system 
designed to provide benefits to employees who suffer work -related injuries 
or illnesses. While the fundamental principles remain consistent, workers' 
compensation details vary by province. Ea ch provincial Workers' 
Compensation Board (WCB) determines specific rules, premium rates, and 
benefit structures. The WCBs operate independently from the government 
and are funded entirely by employer premiums.  You must register with the 
Workers ' Compensat ion Board in your province or territory and follow local 
rules on injury reporting, forms and deadlines. Coverage requirements and 
premiums will vary by province.  
Employer Obligations  
Every employer must register with their provincial WCB and pay insurance 
premiums to cover potential workplace injuries. Employers must report 
workplace injuries to the WCB within 72 hours if the worker needs treatment 
beyond first aid or will miss time from work.  
Injury Reporting and Claims Process  
The claims process is structured to protect the employer and employee. 
Workers have six months from the date of injury or diagnosis to claim 
benefits by reporting their injury or illness to the Workplace Safety and 
Insurance Board (WSIB). The process typic ally involves:  
‚Ä¢ Immediate medical treatment  
‚Ä¢ Reporting the injury to the employer  
‚Ä¢ Documenting the incident  
‚Ä¢ Filing a formal workers' compensation claim  
‚Ä¢ Undergoing medical assessments  
‚Ä¢ Receiving compensation benefits  
Compensation Benefits  
WCB are designed to support injured workers. These benefits typically 
include:  
‚Ä¢ Wage replacement  
‚Ä¢ Medical treatment costs  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -17 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  ‚Ä¢ Rehabilitation services  
‚Ä¢ Permanent disability payments  
‚Ä¢ Survivor benefits in case of fatal workplace accidents  
Eligibility and Coverage  
Not all workers are automatically covered by WCB. Most employees are 
required to carry workers' compensation insurance, certain industries may 
be exempt. Typical WCB coverage includes:  
‚Ä¢ Full-time employees  
‚Ä¢ Part-time workers  
‚Ä¢ Temporary workers  
‚Ä¢ Seasonal employees  
Employer Protections  
The workers' compensation system provides legal protection for employers. 
By participating in the provincial WCB system, employers are generally 
protected from direct civil lawsuits related to workplace injuries. This no -
fault system means employees receiv e benefits regardless of who was 
responsible for the workplace accident.  
Employers must stay informed about their provincial WCB requirements, 
maintain rigorous safety protocols, and ensure prompt and comprehensive 
reporting of any workplace incidents. Proactive workplace safety remains the 
priority.  
Employee Termination Procedures  
Employment law can vary significantly by province and territory. Employers 
should consult their human resources professional or attorney when 
developing termination policies and before proceeding with any complex 
terminations. Regular review and updates of  termination procedures ensure 
ongoing compliance with evolving employment standards.  This summary is 
general; you must consult local laws to ensure compliance with notice 
periods and severance obligations. They may differ from what has been 
provided.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -18 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Documentation Requirements  
Proper documentation is crucial for all terminations. Employers must 
maintain detailed records of:  
‚Ä¢ The reason for termination  
‚Ä¢ Notice provided or pay in lieu of notice  
‚Ä¢ Severance calculations and payments  
‚Ä¢ Final pay including vacation pay  
‚Ä¢ Return of company property issued  
‚Ä¢ Exit interview notes  
Post-Termination Obligations  
Ensure all documentation and obligations are honored following a 
termination. Employer requirements include:  
‚Ä¢ Provide  a Record of Employment within five days of the last day of 
work.  
‚Ä¢ Maintain confidentiality regarding the termination circumstances.  
‚Ä¢ Honor post -employment obligations outlined in employment contracts.  
‚Ä¢ Facilitate the transfer of benefits or pension information.  
‚Ä¢ Provide reference letters, if agreed upon.  
Franchisee Compliance with Labour Laws  
Employer compliance with labour standards, including penalties. When 
employers are not following the Code, the Labour Program uses fair, 
foreseeable, and nationally consistent measures to enforce compliance.  Any 
operational policies in Section E must be adapted to meet local codes and 
human rights requirements. Seek professional guidance from legal or HR 
professionals in your province.  
Workplace Policies  
Creating and maintaining appropriate workplace policies is essential. Develop 
clearly outlined anti -discrimination policies that define prohibited behaviors, 
complaint procedures, and consequences for violations. These policies should 
be easily accessible to all employees and reviewed regularly.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -19 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Include specific examples of both acceptable and unacceptable behavior to 
help employees understand expectations.  
Employment standards legislation can change frequently. Employers should 
establish a system to monitor updates and implement changes promptly to 
maintain compliance with all applicable wage and hour laws.  
Employers should:  
‚Ä¢ Regularly review provincial employment standards updates.  
‚Ä¢ Maintain current wage and hour posting requirements.  
‚Ä¢ Train management staff on proper timekeeping procedures.  
‚Ä¢ Conduct periodic audits of payroll and scheduling practices.  
‚Ä¢ Document all wage -related policies and procedures.  
Discrimination complaints require immediate and comprehensive attention. 
Ensure established protocols are clearly outlined for handling complaints, 
including investigation procedures, and protection against retaliation. All 
complaints should be treated ser iously and confidentially. Document every 
step of the investigation process and maintain secure records of all related 
communications and decisions.  
Training  
Training plays a fundamental role in preventing discrimination. All employees 
should receive regular training on human rights obligations, discrimination 
prevention, and proper handling of accommodation requests. This training is 
to be documented and updat ed as laws and best practices evolve. Always 
keep detailed records of all training sessions, including attendance, and 
content covered.  
Support resources are available to help maintain compliance. Provincial 
Human Rights Commission websites offer region -specific guidance, and the 
Canadian Human Rights Commission provides valuable resources at the 
federal level. Maintain relationships with employment lawyers who specialize 
in human rights law.

evaluating the candidates' res ponses.

the candidate and address any questions they may have.

thinking seriously about whether this job is a good fit.  
Have the candidate fill out an application for your records if no application 
was completed before the interview.

Job Offer  
Once the Owner or Manager has decided to make the official offer and has 
confirmed key terms, the next step involves making the verbal and written 
offer, culminating in the employee's first day as a member of The DRIPBaR 
location's team. Following employme nt, the references and interview rating 
must be retained for up to one year and then may be destroyed. After 
candidate interviews, verification of employment history, and reference 
inquiries, the Owner or Manager is responsible for the employment offer. 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -28 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  After the verbal offer has been made and the candidate has agreed to the 
essential terms of the offer (typically the position, employee classification, 
salary or rate, and the starting date), a written offer will be prepared and 
submitted to the candidate in person or by mail confirming the verbal offer 
and will include the essential terms of the verbal offer as agreed to by the 
candidate.  
The candidate will be required to sign and date an acceptance of the written 
offer that will state as follows: "The undersigned accepts the above 
employment offer and agrees that it contains the terms of employment with 
[insert Franchisee's business entity  name] and that there are no other terms 
express or implied. It is understood that employment is subject to 
verification of identity and employment eligibility and may be terminated by 
[insert Franchisee's business entity name] at any time for any reason."  
The verbal or written offer must never express or imply that employment is 
"permanent," "long -term," of a specific duration, or use words of similar 
meaning. An exception may be made when filling a temporary position of 
known duration. Employers have the o ption to make employment contingent 
upon certain job -related factors, such as obtaining a specific provincial  or 
federal license when appropriate or desirable.  
A Job Offer Letter and Agreement Templates are available in FranConnect. 
Use legal counsel and a human resource vendor to configure the details. The 
Franchisee can and should also look to their HR provider for additional 
support if necessary. ADP is our re commended vendor, although the 
Franchisee can use another vendor if they wish.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  So, review the requirements and expectations with new employees.  
Ensure you comply with all tax requirements:  
1. New and existing employers should consult the Canada Revenue 
Agency  to understand all their federal tax filing requirements. Visit the 
provincial  and local tax page for specific tax filing requirements for 
employers.  
2. Get organized and keep yourself informed.  
Being a good employer does not stop with fulfilling your various tax and 
reporting obligations. Maintaining a healthy and fair workplace, providing 
benefits, and keeping employees informed about your company's policies are 
key to your business's success.  
Payroll Tax Requirements  
Payroll tax requirements can change annually. The Canada Review Agency 
(CRA) provides support through its Payroll Deductions Online Calculator 
(PDOC) to help ensure accurate calculations. Every employer must establish 
and maintain a payroll program account with the CRA. Employers must 
calculate and manage three main types of deductions: Canada Pension Plan 
contributions, Employment Insurance premiums, and income tax. Consult 
with your payroll service.  All withholdings (source deductions) must be 
remitted on the schedule prescribed by the Canada Revenue Agency (CRA). 
You are responsible for keeping updated on a ny changes to CRA thresholds 
or deadlines.  
Canada Pension Plan and Employment Insurance 
Contributions  
Employers have specific obligations regarding Canada Pension Plan (CPP) 
and Employment Insurance (EI) contributions. As of 2024, employers must 
match employee CPP contributions at 5.95% of pensionable earnings. For EI 
premiums, employers must contribute 1.4 times the amount deducted from 
employees.  
 
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                         Human Resources  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page E -31 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Remittance Schedules  
The frequency of tax remittances depends on the average monthly 
withholding amount. For amounts between CA$25,000 and CA$99,999, 
monthly payments are required. For amounts over CA$100,000, remittances 
must be made within three working days. Missing remitta nce deadlines can 
result in penalties, so maintaining a reliable payment schedule is crucial.  
T4 Preparation and Filing  
Annual T4 reporting is required. Verify yearly the deadlines for issuing T4 
slips to employees and CRA filing dates. Employers must ensure all taxable 
income, benefits, and deductions are accurately reported. Electronic filing is 
mandatory for organization s issuing more than five T4 slips.  
Recordkeeping Requirements  
Maintaining accurate and detailed payroll records will help ensure complete 
compliance. Retention periods may vary by province (e.g., Ontario requires 
certain records for 3 years; Alberta requires them for up to 5 years). Check 
local regulations for details. It is up to you to understand your provinces 
requirements. Comprehensive payroll records include:  
‚Ä¢ Employee information and social insurance numbers  
‚Ä¢ Dates and amounts of all remuneration  
‚Ä¢ CPP contributions and EI premium calculations  
‚Ä¢ Income tax deductions  
‚Ä¢ Vacation pay accrual and payments  
‚Ä¢ Records of remittances to CRA  
Tax Forms and Documentation  
Every full -time employee must complete a Personal Tax Credits Return (TD1 
form). New forms are required when an employee's tax situation changes. 
Employers must retain these forms and update payroll calculations 
accordingly when changes occur.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Year -End Procedures  
Maintaining thorough records throughout the calendar year will aid in 
streamlined year -end payroll requirements. At the end of each calendar 
year, Franchisee responsibilities include:  
‚Ä¢ Reconciling payroll accounts.  
‚Ä¢ Verifying year -to-date deduction total.  
‚Ä¢ Preparing and distributing T4 slips by the deadline date.  
‚Ä¢ Filing T4 Summary Forms with the CRA.  
‚Ä¢ Updating employee tax profiles for the new year if claim amounts have 
changed.  
Compliance  
Adhering to payroll laws imposed by relevant governing bodies on all levels 
of government is critical. To ensure compliance, stay current by reviewing 
updates from your payroll service and/or human resources professional.  
Training  
Training ensures that all employees understand and adhere to the Brand 
Standards, ensuring a uniform client experience. Clients expect the same 
service and product quality across all franchise locations, which results in a 
positive reputation. Training pos itively affects the brand's image and can 
enhance operational efficiency by reducing errors and waste.  
Onsite Initial Training  
Prior to opening, a Level 3 Nurse and a member of the Corporate  Training 
Team will arrive at your franchised location to provide two days of onsite 
training, delivered as presentations of The DRIPBaR standards, a hands -on 
experience, and a pop quiz. The training prepares the team hired by the 
Franchisee to begin opera tions. Topics covered include:  
‚Ä¢ Lab operations (reviewing how to set up the lab for USP 
797 compliance, meet protocols, mix drips, and complete electronic 
medical record/EMR documentation)  
‚Ä¢ Front desk functions (the Franchisee and staff will undergo Zenoti 
Training that teaches them how to use the system at the front desk)

take quizzes at the end of each lesson. An  80% or higher is required to pass 
and must be completed before they start working. The lessons are located 
on FranConnect, which consists of 10 plans, with 1 -15 lessons within each 
plan. After completing each plan, a certificate will be awarded.  
As Owner, you have access to every plan.  You are responsible for having 
your staff complete  all training modules.  
Mentor Program  
Mentorship is a professional interaction where an experienced staff member 
(the mentor) imparts their knowledge and expertise to a less experienced 
colleague (the mentee). The mentor provides valuable guidance, advice, 
feedback, and motivation. The mentee,  in turn, has the opportunity to 
discuss personal and professional objectives, queries, and challenges with 
their mentor.  
The Mentor Program is the promotional path for site Nurses and increases 
the retention of staff for Owners. The program's aim is to:  
‚Ä¢ Set a standard training and growth path for the D rip Specialists.  
‚Ä¢ Accelerate the rate of new unit training.  
‚Ä¢ Expand the leaders within The DRIPBaR R&D/Medical Team.

Level 1  
To be a D rip Specialist, The DRIPBaR Brand Standard is a Registered Nurse.  
Level 1 D rip Specialists are fully trained in The DRIPBaR way and can 
perform all operational functions at The DRIPBaR on a day -to-day basis.  
Nurses are starting in the System between $25 and $35/hour, but you may 
need to adjust the pay scale based on your area. After the initial hire, the 
Owner can promote a Registered Nurse to Level 2 as they see fit.  
This is a way to show a prospective Nurse that they start at a point of pay 
and can grow.  
Level 2  
The DRIPBaR Brand Standard for Level 2 is a Registered Nurse or above that 
has met all the standard training for Level 1.  
You are the Lead Nurse at your DRIPBaR. You have the additional 
responsibilities of:  
‚Ä¢ Hood testing  
‚Ä¢ Inventory control  
‚Ä¢ Reviewing the knowledge base of frequently asked questions (FAQs)  
‚Ä¢ Attending weekly Nurse Call  
‚Ä¢ Leading the Level 1 team  
Level 2 is ideal for a Nurse who has been with The DRIPBaR for a minimum 
of six months or has become a larger part of the team, taking more hours, 
and getting great reviews.  
We recommend the Level 2 achievement come with a $2 -$3 pay increase, 
but this is based on the Owner's discretion.

Nurse  
Your location's reputation hinges on the integrity of your Nursing staff.

motivate, and inspire, a great Nurse can attract and retain hundreds of 
members over time.

welcome regardless of their wellness level or reason for their visit.  
A great Nurse is:  
‚Ä¢ Outgoing, welcoming, and personable

members. Nurses should be willing to be flexible, with regular weekend 
availability.  
Recordkeeping for Compliance  
You will need to establish a system of organizing personnel files and 
maintaining the confidentiality of the personal information contained within.  
Note: Personnel files must be kept in a locked file cabinet to protect private 
information.  
Once an applicant is hired, you should immediately establish a personnel file 
for that employee. A personnel file contains:  
‚Ä¢ Completed Application Form  
‚Ä¢ Personal information sheet (including the phone number of someone 
who should be notified in case of an emergency)  
‚Ä¢ Reference letters, if provided  
‚Ä¢ Resume, if applicable  
‚Ä¢ Federal, provincial , and local W -4 Forms  
‚Ä¢ A separate folder should be created for the  eligibility of employees. 
Verify an employee's identity and employment authorization by 
requesting their Social Insurance Number (SIN), which serves a similar 
function in confirming their right to work in Canada. Also i nclude a 
picture identification, i.e., a driver 's license or passport . 
‚Ä¢ Non-Disclosure and Non -Compete Agreement, if applicable  
‚Ä¢ Copy of the license appropriate to their job  
‚Ä¢ Job description  
‚Ä¢ Interview note sheet

and dated)

salary history, and records of disciplinary actions. Within your business, you 
may have additional records to retain.  
Employers must ensure that all staff medical licenses are up  to date. 
Verification systems should be in place to frequently review each license, 
and clear procedures must be set to avoid any oversight that could risk 
client  safety or the business's legal standing.  
A proactive monitoring approach is vital for recognizing soon -to-expire 
licenses, giving practitioners adequate time to renew their professional 
documentation.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Section F: Marketing  
Overview  
Marketing, as one of the key engines driving business growth, is critical to The 
DRIPBaR franchise location 's success. What is marketing? At its very highest 
level, marketing is building relationships that enhance the brand and lead to 
revenue. At The DRIPBaR, branded marketing strategies reflect this 
investment in forming relationships. As you build relationshi ps across client 
groupings, it is important to cast aside the notion that there is a singular, 
magical tactic capable of achieving all client attrac tion, acquisition, and 
retention goals.  
There are a variety of ways to construct relationships, and we will outline 
these in this section. For a more complete discussion, see The DRIPBaR 
Marketing Manual  in SharePoint.  
The DRIPBaR Marketing Philosophy  
At The DRIPBaR, we believe in maximizing potential and using effective 
marketing strategies to raise the bar. The Raise the Bar strategy has three 
components ‚Äî awareness, acquisition, and advocacy ‚Äî each with a series of 
tactics.  
 


DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                                  Marketing  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page F -5 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  By using these tactics simultaneously, we believe you will achieve the proper 
level of consistent awareness for your DRIPBaR location.  
Below, each component of the Raise the Bar strategy will be addressed. Some 
sections will be more detailed than others, yet all are equally important to 
bring into the fold of marketing your DRIPBaR location. See the Marketing 
Manual for full details.  
Aggressive implementation of these marketing strategies and associated 
tactics at the beginning of your DRIPBaR journey will help you to create a 
loyal clientele, early recurring revenue, and extensive brand awareness early 
on. Marketing your DRIPBaR locat ion soon after you sign your lease is 
imperative to the early success of your location 's goals.  
Pre-Opening Plan for Awareness  
The DRIPBaR Pre -Opening Plan (POP) is a strategy designed to generate 
awareness, establish a market presence, generate leads, build anticipation, 
and create momentum before officially opening your doors to the public. The 
DRIPBaR Owners are provided coachi ng, marketing plans, vendor resources, 
print and digital assets, and general support to assist in this opening strategy, 
but ultimately, it is up to the Owner to make sure they are implementing the 
elements necessary for a successful POP.  
The POP is crucial for ensuring a smooth and successful start and employs the 
following campaigns:  
‚Ä¢ Brand Awareness  
‚Ä¢ Client Education  
‚Ä¢ Founder 's Club  
‚Ä¢ Opening Promo  
‚Ä¢ The DRIPBaR Starter Package  
‚Ä¢ First-Time Client Offers  
The POP creates buzz and excitement about your DRIPBaR location with the 
goal of opening to the public with leads, educated clients, and recurring 
revenue.  
After signing your lease, you will be introduced to the Corporate 's Sales and 
Marketing Team and will be educated in the elements of the POP.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                                  Marketing  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page F -6 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Around 90 days prior to opening your DRIPBaR franchised location to the 
public, it is time to implement the POP strategy.  
Key aspects of The DRIPBaR POP that drive awareness and acquisition 
include:  
‚Ä¢ Early Access : Clients are given the chance to purchase packages, join 
the Founder 's Club, and make appointments in advance. This can 
provide them with a sense of exclusivity and the opportunity to be 
among the first to experience The DRIPBaR.  
‚Ä¢ Incentives and Benefits: Special discounts and perks are offered to 
clients during this time. Make sure they know these offers will not be 
available for long! Offers end after the Official Grand Opening.  
‚Ä¢ Reservation or Pre -Order Process: This program establishes a process 
for clients to secure their participation in exclusive offers.  
‚Ä¢ Communication and Marketing: Effective communication and marketing 
are crucial to promote the POP and generate interest. Use emails, 
newsletters, social media, advertisements, influencers, and dedicated 
landing pages to inform clients about the membership program, its 
benefits, and th e upcoming location opening.  
POP Sales Timeline  
The typical new location opening occurs about 120 days after signing the 
lease. Corporate ' Sales Team will spend the first 30 days after signing the 
lease for your new DRIPBaR location working to ensure you are educated and 
prepared to execute the POP strategy. Here is a quick breakdown of what will 
happen once your lease is signed:  
‚Ä¢ 120 Days Out: Send an introduction email and have a call with Sales 
and Marketing Teams.  
‚Ä¢ 110 Days Out: Review POP strategy and select pricing tier. Begin your 
weekly calls with the Sales Team.  
‚Ä¢ 100 Days Out: Test website and POS integration, plus:  
o Select an approved digital agency.  
o Attend meetings with the Sales Team, which will focus on lead 
generation and the importance of events.  
‚Ä¢ 90 Days Out: Start POP campaigns!

‚Ä¢ The goal is to accrue 300+ leads during these 90 -day POP efforts and

POP Campaigns  
The campaigns used during the POP are designed to effectively and efficiently 
take your The DRIPBaR location from the beginning stages of creating buzz, 
all the way to having a full appointment booked.  
The Brand Awareness Campaign  
The Brand Awareness Campaign is an ongoing effort and is without a doubt 
the most important element of any business that wants to have its brand 
known and easily identified. While the brand 's reach is strong, The DRIPBaR is 
new to many people, particularly when opening in a new market.  
Brand awareness is essential for several reasons, as it achieves:  
‚Ä¢ Competitive advantage  
‚Ä¢ Trust and credibility

Building brand awareness takes time, so be patient and stay consistent with

Grassroots Marketing to Build Awareness  
Grassroots marketing leverages the power of local connections, authentic 
engagement, and community involvement to create meaningful relationships, 
drive brand awareness, and establish a strong foundation for business growth 
within specific markets or commu nities.  
Grassroots marketing refers to a strategy that focuses on reaching out to a 
target audience at the local or community level. It centers around non -
traditional, localized, and community -driven efforts. This crucial aspect of 
marketing connects and engages i ndividuals and small groups who will spread 
the message, create a buzz, and advocate for your brand.  
The term "grassroots " implies starting at a "boots on the ground " level rather 
than relying on larger -scale, mainstream marketing channels. It should be 
comprised of low -cost, high -impact tactics that leverage the power of word -of-
mouth, personal connections, and community involvement.  
The impact of grassroots marketing is the result of:  
‚Ä¢ Localized and personalized approach:  Engages with individuals and 
communities on an individual level, resonating with local values, 
preferences, and needs.  
‚Ä¢ Building authentic relationships:  Emphasizes genuine connections and 
interactions, fostering trust and credibility among a targeted audience.  
‚Ä¢ Word -of-mouth advocacy:  Encourages endorsement, promotion, and 
advocacy from satisfied clients or engaged community members, which 
can be highly influential in driving referrals and brand loyalty.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                                  Marketing  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page F -12 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  ‚Ä¢ Cost-effective strategy:  Often relies on low -cost or guerilla tactics, 
leveraging community involvement, partnerships, and creativity, making 
it a cost -effective approach for small businesses or start -ups. 
‚Ä¢ Community engagement:  Actively participates within communities, 
allowing businesses to contribute to local initiatives, events, and causes, 
creating a positive brand image.  
‚Ä¢ Targeted and relevant messaging:  Enables businesses to tailor their 
messaging and offerings to suit the specific needs and interests of the 
local audience, leading to more relevant and impactful communication.  
‚Ä¢ Creating brand advocates:  Engages with individuals directly, so 
businesses can turn satisfied clients or supporters into brand advocates 
who promote the brand organically within their social circles.  
‚Ä¢ Long -term relationship building:  Establishes enduring relationships with 
local communities, laying the groundwork for sustained client loyalty 
and support.  
Grassroots Marketing Types  
A successful location will implement three types of grassroots marketing:  
1. Events, which require a physical presence, including athletic games, 
health and wellness fairs, and bridal shows  
2. Initiatives, which do not require a physical presence, including charity 
contributions and event sponsorships  
3. Partnerships, or ongoing relationships with local businesses, including 
like-minded and nearby businesses  
Events  
A grassroots event typically refers to a gathering or activity organized at a 
local level, driven by individuals, community groups, or small organizations to 
address specific concerns, promote a cause, or advocate for change. These 
events often involve loc al residents, volunteers, or activists who are 
passionate about a particular issue, idea, or movement.  
 
 
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                                  Marketing  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page F -13 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  The DRIPBaR breaks events into two categories: Formal and Informal. Both 
require you to set up a tent or table to collect leads.  
‚Ä¢ Informal Events: These events are cost -effective, but you have less 
control over the demographic. You designate the time and place. For 
example, Pop -up Events are an effective and fun way to hold an 
informal event. A Pop -up Event is a temporary gathering o r experience 
that occurs in a physical space for a limited duration. Gym lobbies, 
vacant lots, galleries, or public areas are all great locations for The 
DRIPBaR Pop -Up Events. These events are known for their novelty, 
creativity, temporary nature, and oft en involve collaboration with like -
minded businesses.  
‚Ä¢ Formal Events: For these events, y ou will typically coordinate through 
an event planner and there may be an entry or sponsorship fee to 
participate. While formal events can be expensive, they allow you more 
control over the type of demographic you will be interacting with. Look 
on Event -Brite or another popular event listing site in your area and see 
what upcoming events are planned! Make a list of events that will have 
pockets of your target audience at them:  
o Health and wellness fairs  
o Athletic events  
o Music/food festivals  
o Local events and celebrations  
o Bridal shows  
Partnerships  
In grassroots marketing, partnerships are instrumental in amplifying 
messages, leveraging shared resources, and mobilizing collective action, 
leading to more successful and impactful campaigns within the community or 
target audience. Examples of partnershi ps include:  
‚Ä¢ Apartments/housing complexes: Create an offer just for their residents.  
‚Ä¢ Healthcare facilities: Help their clients; they can help you get clients.  
‚Ä¢ Like-minded businesses (fitness studios, health food stores, med spas, 
etc.): Seek out places where clients have an affinity for health and 
wellness.  
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Partnerships are beneficial in:  
‚Ä¢ Expanding reach by tapping into each partner 's network, audience, or 
resources, significantly expanding the reach of your marketing efforts.  
‚Ä¢ Building upon the expertise of a partner who brings diverse skills, 
expertise, and perspectives to the initiative, enriching the campaign 's 
creativity and effectiveness.  
‚Ä¢ Sharing resources, such as funding, physical assets, knowledge, or 
workforce, thereby maximizing the impact of limited resources.  
‚Ä¢ Enhancing credibility and trust, particularly if the partners have 
established relationships or influence within the community.  
‚Ä¢ Gaining access to untapped audiences that each partner brings to the 
table, reaching new demographics or segments.  
‚Ä¢ Increasing engagement through collaborative efforts, which often 
fosters higher engagement levels among audiences, as they perceive 
the joint effort as more impactful and credible.  
‚Ä¢ Enabling synergistic campaigns in which partners complement each 
other 's strengths, resulting in a more cohesive and effective marketing 
strategy.  
‚Ä¢ Establishing sustainable relationships that are beneficial not just for one 
campaign but for future initiatives, fostering a sustainable network of 
support and collaboration for your location.  
See The DRIPBaR Marketing Manual for approaches to establishing successful 
partnerships within your community.  
Initiatives  
A grassroots initiative refers to a movement, project, or action that originates 
at the local level, often initiated by individuals, community groups, or small 
organizations to address a specific issue, create change, or promote a cause 
within a community or society. Examples of initiatives include:  
‚Ä¢ Cause Marketing aligns your The DRIPBaR location with a social or 
environmental cause. Your location actively supports this cause through 
partnerships or donations that resonate with consumers who are 
passionate about those issues. This grassroots initiati ve demonstrates a 
commitment to making a positive impact and can attract like -minded 
individuals to the brand.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                                  Marketing  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page F -15 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  ‚Ä¢ Open House provides an opportunity to introduce your new business to 
your local community and target audience. By inviting people to visit 
your The DRIPBaR location, you create awareness about your products, 
services, and offerings. This allows potential c lients, neighbors, and 
other community members to learn firsthand about The DRIPBaR.  
‚Ä¢ Guerilla Marketing is an unconventional marketing approach that 
involves creating memorable and surprising experiences in public 
spaces. It often includes activities such as graffiti, flash mobs, public 
stunts, or installations that capture attention and g enerate buzz through 
social sharing and word -of-mouth.  
‚Ä¢ Street Teams are enthusiastic individuals who hit the streets to promote 
your products, services, and cause through direct interactions with 
potential clients and supporters. Street Team Members distribute 
coupons, flyers, promotional materials, and engage  in conversations to 
raise awareness and generate interest.  
Initiatives are beneficial, in that they have:  
‚Ä¢ Local Origin:  They start from the ground level, emerging from the ideas, 
concerns, or needs of individuals or small groups within a community.  
‚Ä¢ Bottom -Up Approach:  They are driven by community members or 
stakeholders, rather than by government bodies, large organizations, or 
corporations.  
‚Ä¢ Community Engagement:  Initiatives happen through active 
participation, engagement, and collaboration among local residents, 
volunteers, activists, or concerned citizens who are passionate about a 
particular cause or issue.  
‚Ä¢ Advocacy or Change:  Often they aim to bring attention to an issue or to 
drive social, political, environmental, or cultural change.  
‚Ä¢ Limited Resources:  Initiatives typically rely on community support, 
volunteer efforts, creativity, and passion to achieve their goals.  
‚Ä¢ Organic Growth:  They often gain momentum through word -of-mouth, 
social networks, or local media coverage.  
‚Ä¢ Community Impact:  They address concerns or bring about change that 
directly affects the lives of community members.

Referral Programs for Acquisition  
Solid, planned -out referral programs are a crucial aspect of obtaining new 
clients and driving revenue. Current members and clients, staff, affiliates, and 
other healthcare providers are the leading pathways to new clients. Therefore, 
forming a solid relationship with your clients and the community is essential to 
growing The DRIPBaR location.  
Typically, in the health and wellness vertical, 35 -55% of all clients and 
members come from some form of referral. The majority of your location 's 
clients should come from referrals over all other marketing tactics. To attain 
this, it is imperative to develop protocols and methodologies to maximize 
referral potential.  
Depending on the stage of The DRIPBaR location and the credibility you have 
built in the community, the focus on these programs will vary. If your location 
is new, introducing your The DRIPBaR to the community, building your brand, 
and establishing professional credibility are paramount to success. There is no 
magic wand or any one tactic that will speed up the expansion of your referral 
network or build your brand and credibility ‚Äî it is a process with multiple 
steps. When the steps are taken and executed appropriately, you will 
experience gratifying results.

Enlist a Client Advocacy Manager  
The Client Advocacy Manager (CAM) or Community Relations Director (CRD) is

should immerse themselves into the community and execute a plan t o build 
solid relationships.  
Quite often, franchise Owners assume the CAM/CRD role at the onset, as the 
face of the brand. Owners who have a large presence in the community are 
able to propel awareness to future alliances and clients.

6. Pitching the Concept

The Five DRIPBaR Referral Programs  
There are five key referral programs that build your referral network and 
provide incentives for staff to develop relationships and get comfortable with 
making an "ask." These programs, along with the suggested incentives and 
collateral kits, will provide support to your efforts and implementation. The 
more focus and resources applied to these programs and steps, the more 
optimal the results in acquiring a preferred clien t. 
Learn about each referral program below. Specific guidance and support in 
building your referral network can be found in The DRIPBaR Marketing 
Manual.  
Client Referral Program  
The client referral program is a marketing strategy designed to encourage 
current clients to refer new clients to The DRIPBaR location. It is a way for 
you to leverage the positive experiences and satisfaction of your current 
clients to attract new ones.  
In the client referral program, incentives are offered to clients who refer 
potential clients to  The DRIPBaR.  
Client referral programs can be beneficial in several ways:  
‚Ä¢ They can generate new leads and clients at a relatively low cost 
compared to traditional marketing and advertising methods.  
‚Ä¢ Referred clients tend to have a higher level of trust in the business 
because the recommendation comes from someone they know. This can 
lead to higher conversion rates and client loyalty.  
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                                  Marketing  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page F -20 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  ‚Ä¢ Client referral programs can help foster a sense of community and 
engagement among existing drippers, as they become active 
participants in promoting The DRIPBaR. Successful client referral 
programs rely on clear communication and easy -to-use referral 
mech anisms. Regular tracking and monitoring of referrals and rewards 
are also essential to ensure transparency and fairness in the program.  
Overall, the client referral program can be a powerful tool to help you tap into 
the network and goodwill of your existing clients, resulting in increased 
acquisition, retention, and business growth.  
Member Referral Program  
The member referral program is a strategy implemented to encourage your 
existing members to refer new members or clients. It is a way to show your 
members a higher level of appreciation and to leverage the loyalty and 
satisfaction of your current members t o attract new ones. Member referrals 
should have a higher level of incentivization in order to show members  an 
even stronger gesture of appreciation.  
In a member referral program, existing members are incentivized to refer 
friends, family, or acquaintances to become new clients or members. In the 
member referral program, incentives are offered to members who refer 
potential clients to The DRIPBaR.  
Member referral programs can be beneficial in several ways:  
‚Ä¢ They can generate new leads and clients at a relatively low cost 
compared to traditional marketing and advertising methods.  
‚Ä¢ Referrals tend to have a higher level of trust in the business because the 
recommendation comes from someone they know or trust. This can lead 
to higher conversion rates and client loyalty.  
‚Ä¢ Member referral programs can help foster a sense of community and 
engagement among existing drippers, as they become active 
participants in promoting The DRIPBaR.  
Successful member referral programs rely on clear communication and easy -
to-use referral mechanisms. Regular tracking and monitoring of referrals and 
rewards are also essential to ensure transparency and fairness in the 
program.  
Overall, the client referral program can be a powerful tool to help you tap into 
the network and goodwill of your existing clients, resulting in increased 
acquisition, retention, and business growth.

Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                                  Marketing  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page F -21 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Staff Referral Program  
A staff referral program, also known as an employee incentive program, is a 
structured initiative designed to motivate and reward DRIPBaR employees for 
achieving specific goals or demonstrating exceptional performance. It is a way 
for organizations to recognize and appreciate the efforts of their employees 
and encourage them to bring new cli ents in.  
Staff referral programs involve the implementation of rewards and incentives 
that are tied to individual or team performance.  
These rewards can take different forms, such as financial bonuses, salary 
increases, gift cards, extra time off, recognition and awards, career 
advancement opportunities, training and development programs, or non -
monetary perks like flexible work arrangeme nts or special privileges.  
To create an effective staff incentive program:  
‚Ä¢ Establish clear and measurable goals that employees can strive to 
achieve.  
‚Ä¢ Provide a fair and transparent framework for tracking and evaluating 
performance.  
‚Ä¢ Communicat e to ensure  that employees understand the program 's 
objectives, criteria for rewards, and the performance metrics used.  
‚Ä¢ Ensure that the incentives offered are meaningful and aligned with  
employees ' needs and desires. Tailoring rewards to individual 
preferences or providing a range of options can help increase motivation 
and engagement.  
‚Ä¢ Provide r egular evaluation and feedback to ensure the success of a staff 
incentive program.  
Care should be taken to avoid creating unhealthy competition, fostering a 
sense of entitlement, or inadvertently encouraging unethical behavior. It is 
crucial to strike a balance between recognizing and rewarding employees 
while maintaining a collaborative  and supportive work environment.  
Practitioner Referral Program  
A practitioner referral program is a strategy used to encourage other 
healthcare professionals to refer clients to The DRIPBaR location. It is a way 
for practitioners to leverage their professional networks and build a mutually 
beneficial relationship with  you. 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                                  Marketing  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page F -22 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  In the practitioner referral program, you will actively seek referrals from other 
practitioners who may encounter clients who require services that are outside 
of their own expertise or scope of practice. The program typically involves 
establishing formal or informal partnerships, where practitioners agree to 
refer clients to one another based on their respective specialties and  areas of 
expertise.  
The referral process in a practitioner referral program usually involves direct 
communication between practitioners, either through personal referrals, 
phone calls, emails, or referral management systems. The referring 
practitioner provides information abo ut the client 's needs and recommends 
the receiving practitioner as a trusted and competent provider.  
The benefits of a practitioner referral program are numerous : 
‚Ä¢ It allows practitioners to expand their client base by tapping into the 
networks of other professionals.  
‚Ä¢ Referrals from trusted colleagues often result in higher -quality leads, as 
potential clients are more likely to have confidence in the recommended 
practitioner.  
‚Ä¢ Referrals can enhance the reputation and credibility of your location, as 
The DRIPBaR is being endorsed by people they trust with their health.  
It is common for practitioners to reciprocate referrals in a referral program, 
creating a two -way referral network. However, the specifics of reciprocity can 
vary depending on the practitioners ' agreement and the nature of their 
respective practices.  
It is important to note that ethical considerations and professional guidelines 
should be followed in a practitioner referral program. Practitioners should 
ensure that referrals are made in the best interest of the client and are not 
driven solely by finan cial incentives. Transparent and ethical practices help 
maintain the integrity and trustworthiness of the referral program.  
Overall, a well -executed practitioner referral program can be a valuable 
marketing and business development strategy for professionals. It can help 
practitioners expand their network, increase client acquisition, and build 
collaborative relationships withi n their industry.  
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                                  Marketing  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page F -23 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Corporate Partnership Referral Program  
This is a collaborative initiative between The DRIPBaR and one or more 
companies or organizations who form a strategic partnership and engage in 
joint marketing and sales efforts. It involves creating an alliance where each 
partner promotes and sells the products or services of the other partner(s) in 
exchange for agreed -upon benefits or incentives.  
Participating companies typically become affiliates of one another, meaning 
they actively promote each other 's products or services through various 
marketing channels.  
This promotion  can include sharing referral links, displaying banner ads, 
creating co -branded marketing materials, social media posts, or other forms 
of collaborative marketing campaigns.  
Key aspects commonly found in an affiliate alliance program include:  
‚Ä¢ Partner Identification:  Companies identify and select partners that have 
complementary products or services, target similar audiences, or 
operate in related industries. The partners should have a mutual 
interest in cross -promoting each other to leverage their respective 
customer  bases and expand market reach.  
‚Ä¢ Affiliate Promotion:  Each partner actively promotes the products or 
services of the other partner(s) through their marketing channels. This 
can include websites, social media platforms, email newsletters, blog 
posts, or other advertising mediums. Affiliates typically use uniq ue 
referral links or codes to track the leads and sales generated from their 
promotional efforts.  
‚Ä¢ Commission or Incentive Structure:  Partners agree on the commission 
or incentive structure for the affiliate program. This outlines the 
compensation or rewards each partner will receive for the sales or leads 
generated through their referrals. The structure can be based on a 
percentage of sales, a fixed fee per referral, or other mutually agreed -
upon terms.  
‚Ä¢ Tracking and Analytics:  Effective tracking and analytics mechanisms are 
put in place to monitor the performance of the affiliate program. This 
includes tracking the number of clicks, conversions, and sales generated 
by each partner 's promotional efforts. The partners often utilize affiliate 
tracking software or platforms to manage the program effectively.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  A corporate partnership offers several benefits toparticipating companies. It 
allows them to tap into each other 's customer base, expanding their reach 
and potential market share. Additionally, it can result in increased brand 
exposure, higher website traffic, and improved sales and revenue for both 
partners.  
To ensure the success of a corporate partnership, it is important to establish 
clear expectations, provide comprehensive training and support to affiliates, 
and maintain open communication. Regular performance evaluation, 
feedback, and adjustments to the p rogram are necessary to optimize results.  
Ethical considerations and transparency are essential in corporate 
partnerships. Each participating business should promote each other 's 
products or services honestly and with integrity, ensuring that their audience 
receives accurate information and fair recommendations.  
Overall, corporate partnerships can be a valuable strategy for companies to 
collaborate, leverage their marketing efforts, and mutually benefit from each 
other 's customer base and expertise.

and credibility within their network.  
‚Ä¢ Referrals and Recommendations:  Through networking, small businesses 
can receive referrals and recommendations from their connections, 
generating leads and expanding their customer base through word -of-
mouth.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Public Relations for Awareness of New Location  
Public relations involves  managing the communication and relationships 
between an organization and its audience, aiming to create a positive public 
image, convey key messages, and build mutually beneficial connections 
through strategic communication efforts. It encompasses various  tactics such 
as media relations, community engagement, crisis management, and 
storytelling to influence perceptions and maintain favorable relationships.  
As a new business with a concept that is relatively new to many people, public 
relations are particularly important to enhance brand awareness and create 
anticipation.  
Similar to other marketing efforts, public relations ha s many benefits, in that 
it: 
‚Ä¢ Establishes credibility and builds trust.  
‚Ä¢ Creates brand awareness.  
‚Ä¢ Is cost -effective marketing compared to paid advertising.  
‚Ä¢ Aids in managing public perception by addressing any negative 
perceptions or misconceptions about the brand.  
‚Ä¢ Facilitates building relationships with consumers, suppliers, and the local 
community.  
‚Ä¢ Helps in crisis management by mitigating potential damage to the 
brand 's reputation.  
‚Ä¢ Cultivates media relationships with journalists, bloggers, and 
influencers.  
‚Ä¢ Complement s marketing initiatives by providing third -party validation 
campaigns.  
Public relations and subsequent media coverage can significantly impact brand 
exposure.  
Please review the Public Relations Section of The DRIPBaR Marketing Manual 
for guidance and common media questions.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Content Marketing: Another Awareness Strategy  
Content marketing is a strategic marketing approach focused on creating and 
distributing valuable, relevant, and consistent content to attract and retain a 
targeted audience. The primary goal of content marketing is to engage 
potential customers, build bra nd awareness, drive profitable consumer action, 
and establish the brand as an authoritative and trustworthy resource within its 
industry or niche.  
Content marketing can take various forms, including articles, blog posts, 
videos, social media posts, infographics, podcasts, and more, tailored to 
address the interests and needs of the intended audience.  
Executing content marketing involves several key steps, and it is suggested 
that you work with your digital marketing agency, social media vendor, and 
website team to assist you with this.  
Social Media Policy  
At The DRIPBaR, we understand that social media can be a fun and rewarding 
way to share your life and opinions with family, friends, and co -workers 
around the world. However, the use of social media also presents certain risks 
and carries with it certain r esponsibilities.  
To assist you in making responsible decisions about your use of social media, 
we have established these guidelines for the appropriate use of social media. 
This policy applies to all associates who work for The DRIPBaR.  
Guidelines  
In the rapidly expanding world of electronic communication, social media can 
mean many things. Social media includes all means of communicating or 
posting information or content of any sort on the internet. This includes your 
own or someone else's web page , blog, journal, social networking site, web 
bulletin board, or chatroom ‚Äî whether or not it is associated or affiliated with 
The DRIPBaR.  
Before creating online content, consider some of the risks and rewards that 
are involved. Keep in mind that any of your conduct that adversely affects 
your job performance, the performance of fellow associates, or otherwise 
adversely affects members, clien ts, vendors, or the interests of anyone else 
who works on behalf of The DRIPBaR may result in disciplinary action.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                                  Marketing  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page F -28 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  ‚Ä¢ Post appropriately: Inappropriate postings that may include 
discriminatory remarks, harassment, threats of violence, or similar 
inappropriate or unlawful conduct will not be tolerated and will subject 
you to disciplinary action, up to and including termina tion. 
‚Ä¢ Comment appropriately: Commenting appropriately on social media is 
essential for fostering a positive online environment. When engaging in 
discussions or expressing opinions, it is crucial to be respectful and 
considerate of others ' perspectives. Avoid offensive language, personal 
attacks, or any form of harassment in order to contribute to healthier 
online discourse. Commenting on other people 's posts to strictly 
promote something unrelated is not allowed. Remember that social 
media is a diverse space with  users holding various beliefs and 
backgrounds, so fostering open -mindedness and empathy in your 
comments promotes a more inclusive and tolerant digital community.  
‚Ä¢ Be respectful: Always be fair and courteous to fellow associates, clients, 
members, vendors, and people who work on behalf of The DRIPBaR. 
Keep in mind that you are more likely to resolve complaints by utilizing 
the Open -Door Policy and speaking directly w ith your employer and/or 
co-workers rather than by posting complaints to a social media outlet.  
‚Ä¢ Nevertheless, if you decide to post complaints or criticism, avoid using 
statements, photographs, video, or audio that reasonably could be 
viewed as malicious, obscene, threatening, or intimidating; that 
disparages clients, members, associates, or vendors;  or that might 
constitute harassment or bullying. Examples of such conduct might 
include offensive posts meant to intentionally harm someone 's 
reputation or posts that could contribute to a hostile work environment 
on the basis of race, sex, disability, re ligion, or any other status 
protected by law or company policy.  
‚Ä¢ Be honest and accurate: Make sure you are always honest and accurate 
when posting information or news, and if you make a mistake, correct it 
quickly. Be open about any previous posts you have altered. Remember 
that the internet archives almost everything; therefore, even deleted 
postings can be searched. Never post any information or rumors that 
you know to be false about The DRIPBaR, fellow associates, members, 
clients, vendors, people working on behalf of The DRIPBaR, or 
competitors.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  ‚Ä¢ Post only appropriate and respectful content:  
o Maintain the confidentiality of The DRIPBaR trade secrets and 
private or confidential information. Trade secrets may include 
information regarding the development of systems, processes, 
products, know -how, and technology. Do not post internal reports, 
policies, procedures, or other internal business -related confidential 
communications.  
o Respect financial disclosure laws. It is illegal to communicate or 
give a "tip" on inside information to others so that they may buy 
or sell stocks or securities. Such online conduct may also violate 
the Insider Trading Policy.  
o Do not create a link from your blog, website, or other social 
networking site to The DRIPBaR website without identifying 
yourself as a The DRIPBaR associate.  
o If expressing personal opinions, never represent yourself as a 
spokesperson for The DRIPBaR. If The DRIPBaR is the subject of 
the content you are creating, be clear and open about the fact 
that you are an associate and make it clear that your views do not 
represent those of The DRIPBaR, fellow associates, members, 
clients, vendors, or people working on behalf of The DRIPBaR. If 
you do publish a blog or post online related to the work you do or 
subjects associated with The DRIPBaR, make it clear that you are  
not speaking on behalf of The DRIPBaR. It is best to include a 
disclaimer such as, "The postings on this site are my own and do 
not necessarily reflect the views of The DRIPBaR. " 
‚Ä¢ QR codes: Please do not put QR codes on anything digital!  
o About 90% of The DRIPBaR digital assets will be seen on a mobile 
device. QR codes are unusable on mobile devices.  
o When a consumer sees a QR code on a social media post, they will 
immediately know that whoever posted that is not tech savvy. 
This will reduce your brand 's credibility.  
o QR codes should only be on print materials or other forms of 
digital media, such as a streaming service commercial or a 
billboard ‚Äî in other words, on something that would not typically 
be seen on a phone.

Digital Marketing for Awareness and Acquisition  
Digital marketing involves using digital channels, such as social media, 
websites, email, search engines, and other digital platforms to promote 
products, services, and brand recognition.  
It involves various strategies and tactics to reach and engage with a target 
audience, aiming to drive traffic, leads, and ultimately business growth. While 
digital marketing is an important tactic to market The DRIPBaR location, it 
should not be relied up on in and of itself.  
All of the various digital marketing aspects will propel each other, so making 
sure they all overlap and work together is imperative to optimizing results.  
Remember: Someone needs to see your brand at least six to seven times 
before they take action. Digital marketing helps this process move quicker by 
ensuring a social media and Google presence.  
Digital marketing must be a part of your marketing mix, but make sure to not 
overemphasize it. Remember that digital advertising probably will only 
account for a percentage of your overall business, so over -focusing on this 
one tactic could be detrimental to your overall marketing efforts, especially if 
you are placing more time and resources into this tactic than needed.  
It is important for a Franchisee to use an approved digital marketing agency, 
because doing so ensures adherence to The DRIPBaR 's Brand Standards, 
consistency in messaging, and maximizes the effectiveness of digital 
marketing efforts. Working with an approved digital marketing agency 
ensures:  
‚Ä¢ Brand Consistency:  Franchises operate under a brand with specific 
guidelines, values, and messaging. Approved digital marketing agencies 
are well -versed in these Brand Standards and ensure that all marketing 
campaigns align with the Franchisor 's image, voice, and values. 
Consistency across different franchise locations builds brand recognition 
and trust among clients.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  ‚Ä¢ Expertise in Franchise Marketing:  Approved agencies have experience 
working with franchises. They understand the nuances of franchise

targeting, and strategies that appeal to local audiences while

‚Ä¢ Access to Resources and Tools:  Approved agencies have access to

‚Ä¢ Compliance and Support:  Using an approved agency ensures 
compliance with Franchisor regulations and marketing policies. These 
agencies have a working relationship with the Franchisor and are 
familiar with any specific requirements or restrictions. Additionally, they 
might provid e ongoing support, training, or assistance related to the 
Franchisor 's marketing strategies.  
‚Ä¢ Efficiency and Cost -Effectiveness:  Approved agencies are accustomed 
to working within franchise systems, which can lead to more efficient 
workflows. They understand the processes and requirements, potentially 
leading to cost -effective solutions  and r eturn on investment.

Required Marketing Approval  
Keep The DRIPBaR brand strong ! As a new franchise, it is imperative that 
brand guidelines are followed. Getting creative approval is important for 
making sure your materials reflect the brand appropriately.  
Creative approval is essential for a franchise to maintain brand consistency, 
uphold Brand Standards, and protect the overall brand identity across various 
locations.  
Here is why gaining approval is necessary:  
‚Ä¢ Brand Consistency:  Franchises have strict brand guidelines that dictate 
how the brand should be represented visually and tonally. Creative 
approval ensures that all marketing materials, advertisements, or 
promotional content align with these guidelines, maintaining a 
consis tent brand image across the franchise network.  
‚Ä¢ Protecting Brand Identity:  Adherence to Brand Standards helps protect 
the franchise 's identity, ensuring that its values, messaging, and visual 
elements are conveyed accurately, reinforcing the brand 's recognition 
and reputation.  
‚Ä¢ Quality Control:  Creative approval ensures that marketing materials 
meet a certain quality standard. It prevents inconsistencies, errors, or 
misleading information that could negatively impact the brand 's 
perception among customers.  
‚Ä¢ Legal and Compliance Requirements:  As a medical franchise, there are 
legal and regulatory requirements that need to be met in marketing 
materials. Creative approval helps ensure that all content complies with 
these regulations.
