Why IV Vitamin Therapy?  
Micronutrient deficiency among American adults has been on the rise  and 
this trend will continue; researchers believe this has contributed to  the 
higher occurrence of chronic diseases  and inflammation a s well as a 
decrease  in immunity.  
Given today's fast -paced lifestyle, over -consumption of processed  foods, 
exposure to chemicals, and common use of gastric bypass surgery  and PPIs 
(protein pump  inhibitors:  Prevacid, Prilosec, Nexium), the traditional ways 
of maintaining optimal health, such as eating a balanced diet and  exercising 
regularly, are harder to sustain and often not enough  to achieve optimum 
health . 
The DRIPBaR aims to support a long, healthy, vital lifespan that is resilient 
to disease. We know that individual cells are recognized as the building 
blocks of the body. By targeting cells for rejuvenation, we believe that the 
body's organs and functional system can be better maintained. Furthermore, 
the CellVie Theory supports IV vitamin therapy ‚Äî when micronutrients are 
applied directly through the vein to target cells, the opportunity exists to 
improve and strengthen cellular heal th in a way that can re duce disease 
outcomes and support general vitality.  
The previous description drives The DRIPBaR business model generally. But 
the key to The DRIPBaR sales process is understanding the client 's personal 
"why" ‚Äî what motivates them to seek IV vitamin therapy.  
Who Are Our Clients?  
The categories of The DRIPBaR clients are outlined below:  
‚Ä¢ Young, healthy, active individuals ranging from 30 -50 years  old, who 
are seeking  lifestyle  infusions to  enhance energy,  to recover  from 
excessive  social  activity or athletic  activity,  or to support 
their health  through times of colds,  flu, stress, or  traveling . 
‚Ä¢ Middle -aged individuals ranging from 40 -70 years old, who are more 
aware of possible or  current medical conditions including  elevated 
cholesterol, high blood  pressure, and cardiovascular issues.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                             Sales  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page G -4 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  o This demographic fundamentally  feels healthy but  has 
become  concerned about long -term consequences.  
‚Ä¢ Individuals with active medical  conditions:  
o Most will range from 40 -70 years old , but may include older 
individuals. This  group includes those who have had  strokes, 
heart attacks, cancer,  impaired memory, Parkinson's, 
chronic  autoimmune diseases, or  gastrointestinal problems.  
o Locations will be able to increase  their volume by educating 
local healthcare practitioners about the  services that they have 
available for this category.  
The typical The DRIPBaR client base has these characteristics:  
‚Ä¢ Equally male and female  
‚Ä¢ 30 years or older  
‚Ä¢ Educated  
‚Ä¢ Middle - to upper -class 
‚Ä¢ Prioritizes a healthy lifestyle  
‚Ä¢ May have a chronic condition  
Individual Clients as a Revenue Stream  
The most difficult revenue stream  to build is  individual clients, especially in 
the early days of your location. These clients germinate from prospects who 
have not been a client of The DRIPBaR and are being introduced to the 
brand for the first time. They receive offers and are served up primarily 
through advertising. These first timers are making a leap of faith in trying 
The DR IPBaR and IV Therapy. These potential clients must have a 
compelling reason to try The DRIPBaR for the first time and to become 
actual clients.  
Perhaps these potential clients have had IV Therapy in the past and they are 
now looking for a convenient and credible establishment to switch to, but 
what also needs to be considered is the prospects who have never 
experienced IV Therapy before. This is why education about IV Therapy and 
The DRIPBaR is so important as a part of the sales approach.

Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                             Sales  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page G -5 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Sales Strategy  
During The DRIPBaR  onboarding process, you will be in contact with the 
Head of Sales and the Director of Sales to discuss in depth The DRIPBaR 
sales strategy and resources to take advantage of. The following is an 
overview of The DRIPBaR sales strategy.  
The Marketing 3 Ps  
The marketing "3 Ps" refers to product, price, and promotional strategy, 
which are the essential components for establishing a strong market 
presence. Together, these elements help create a robust marketing mix that 
can drive sales and build brand loyalty.  
The Product  
A successful product strategy involves offering services that fulfill clients ' 
needs and stand out from the competition. So, instead of saying what 
services we offer (what the product is), think about why we offer the service 
and the problem The DRIPBaR solves for the leads.  For example, a client is 
looking to try The DRIPBaR servic es and says, "I was interested in your 
services and had a specific question about hydration. My doctor said I do not 
drink enough water. Although I try my best to do this, I often do not hit my 
water intake goals. Do you have anything that can help me to s tay better 
hydrated?" You can respond with, "We have many, but if you are looking for 
hydration, we can offer the Hydration Drip." This shows a human -centered 
approach to pitching to your clients why they should choose to obtain a 
service from The DRIPBaR.  
Know that your leads are comparing The DRIPBaR to other services. You 
know your organization best and need to show them why it is the better 
option.  
What makes The DRIPBaR client experience unique from other competitors? 
Although the services may be similar, The DRIPBaR is unique because we:  
‚Ä¢ Promote cellular/preventative health.  
‚Ä¢ Create a spa -like experience for clients.  
‚Ä¢ Have USP 797 compliance incorporated into standards.  
‚Ä¢ Only hire Registered Nurses to perform services.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                             Sales  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page G -6 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  ‚Ä¢ Create exclusivity for clientele by offering memberships and packages 
to purchase.  
Building rapport is pivotal to cultivating a trusted relationship with potential 
clients. When the Sales Team Members take the time to understand and 
connect with leads on a personal level, they create a comfortable and 
supportive environment that reflects  an exclusive atmosphere. Some 
recommended questions to build trust with leads:  
‚Ä¢ Where are you from?  
‚Ä¢ What kind of work do you do?  
‚Ä¢ Do you have any plans this weekend?  
‚Ä¢ Have you been to ______?  
‚Ä¢ The following questions are recommended to make the sale:  
‚Ä¢ What made you interested in a drip?  
‚Ä¢ How would this impact your [energy, stress level, or sleep]?  
‚Ä¢ What is your current wellness routine?  
With this knowledge, you convert leads to sales through the SUPS tactic:  
‚Ä¢ S - What is your goal? ( Specific Goal)  
o For example:  
‚ñ™ "I want to lose weight" - Not Specific  
‚ñ™ "I want to lose 15 pounds by July 1st for a wedding I am 
attending." - Specific  
‚Ä¢ U - Why is that your goal? ( Underlying Motivation). The underlying 
motivation in this example is stated by the client ‚Äî they are in an 
upcoming wedding and want to look a certain way in pictures or fit into 
a particular outfit.  
‚Ä¢ P - Have you done IV therapy in the past? ( Past Experience). Asking, 
"Have you ever done a drip before?" is also part of the discovery 
process. The key here is to gather as much pertinent information as 
possible to later be used to close the sale.  
‚Ä¢ S - "Well, now that I know your goals, let me tell you what I would 
recommend, and then I would love to get you scheduled." ( Schedule).

The Price  
Price is the value that customers are willing to pay for a product, and it must 
be set strategically to balance profitability with customer satisfaction.  
Promotional Strategy

services offered.

increases the conversion rates. By meticulously monitoring each stage a lead 
goes through, from initial awareness to the membership purchase decision, 
you gain valuable insights into clients ' behavior and preferences, as well as 
the effectiveness of the sales process.

Lead Management Cadence  
Having a lead management cadence is crucial for businesses because it 
ensures that potential clients are engaged with the right frequency and 
through the most effective channels. This structured approach to lead 
nurturing helps in maintaining a clear commu nication timeline, which in turn 
increases the likelihood of converting leads into clients.

Remember, h ow you say it is  just as important as what you say. As a health 
and wellness franchise, we must be careful not to give guarantees or false 
claims.  
Say    Do Not Say  
"May ‚Ä¶ "   "Can ‚Ä¶ " 
"Might ‚Ä¶ "   "Will ‚Ä¶ " 
"Is designed to ‚Ä¶ " "Cure ‚Ä¶ " 
When in doubt, use a disclaimer like "This is a truthful report from an actual 
client , but does not guarantee you will achieve the same outcome ‚Äî each 
situation varies. " 
Sales Cycle in Store  
 
 The Sales Cycle follows this pattern:  
1. The lead comes into the location and "Introduction is Conducted."  
2. The Front Desk/Salesperson will "Hand Off" the client to the Nurse . 
3. After the service, the Drip Nurse will "Hand Back" the client to the 
Front Desk/Salesperson.  


DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                             Sales  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page G -15 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  4. Front Desk/Salesperson will "Close the Sale" (including Review, 
Referral, and Rebook).  
The introduction consists of a warm welcome, plus a rundown on what will 
happen on the day. For example: "Gail, we are first going to have you fill out 
some basic medical paperwork, after that we will have Nurse Becky take 
your vitals and then get your bag  of nutrients  mixed and started for you. " 
This Introduction could also include a brief tour of the facility. We would also 
conduct SUPS at this stage in the process ‚Äî explore the client 's Specific 
Goal, Underlying Motivation, Past Experience, and Schedule.  
During the hand off from the Front Desk to the Nurse, the Front Desk staff 
communicates with the Nurse. The Front Desk staff shares which service(s) 
the client is scheduled for that day and a brief needs analysis.  
This needs analysis inform s the Nurse 's dialogue with the client during their 
drip experience.  
During the hand back, the Nurse would give a rundown of which services 
they recommended to the client. Knowing these recommendations helps the 
Front Desk Associate close the sale.  
The three R 's ‚Äî review, referral, and rebook ‚Äî are important for recurring 
revenue. Therefore, it is important to keep the three R 's top of your mind 
throughout the entire sales process.  
The Role of the Nurses in Sales  
It is crucial that the Nurses embrace and take part in your sales efforts. 
They are the experts, they will have the most contact with the client, and 
they will likely be the determining reason someone decides to come back.  
Their objective is to educate, to establish trust, and to exemplify why The 
DRIPBaR stands out. Unlike a gym or a smoothie shop, not all consumers 
know what they will get when they come to The DRIPBaR. Emphasis on 
education not only informs potential clien ts of what you offer, but also helps 
build trust, credibility, and awareness; ultimately , education drives informed 
decisions and foster s a positive reputation within the industry.  
Many people may have misconceptions or limited knowledge about vitamin 
therapy. Education helps dispel myths, clarify doubts, and provide accurate 
information, fostering a better understanding of the therapy. Educated 
consumers are more likely to make info rmed decisions. Potential clients can 
assess the suitability of vitamin therapy for their needs.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                             Sales  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page G -16 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Education showcases the expertise and knowledge of your business. It 
positions the brand as a reliable source of information and expertise in the 
field of vitamin therapy. Educational content fosters engagement and trust, 
leading to stronger and long er-lasting relationships with clients who value 
the information and guidance provided by the business.  
Trust forms the foundation of strong client relationships. When clients trust 
the business, they are more likely to engage repeatedly and recommend the 
services to others.  
Memberships  
The DRIPBaR membership model promotes ongoing relationships with clients 
who enjoy being part of an exclusive club.  
While memberships can come from advertising and other tactics, the more 
cost-effective way to acquire a member is by having your staff upsell an 
individual client into a membership. Additional revenue should not just come 
from new clients, but from current  clients spending more money with you, 
thus increasing the long -term value of a client.  
Your location should build tactics to maximize an individual client converting 
into a member. To accomplish this, building a robust database profile of your 
clients is imperative. If staff, Nurses, and Owners pay attention to each 
individual client and inp ut data to help form a more intimate relationship 
with the client, conversion into a member will be much easier and more 
successful. Each time a client visits, the staff, Nurses, or Owners should be 
collecting three new "tidbits " about the client. This wil l create the proper 
data to reference to make people feel special and solidify the relationship.  
Customers and clients alike want to feel comfortable with the businesses 
they are frequenting. The more you make your clients feel comfortable and a 
part of The DRIPBaR family, the greater the likelihood that they will spend 
more time and money with you. I t is important to remember that while 
acquiring new customers is great and important, spending all your focus on 
prospects is a mistake. Why? Prospects can bring you one thing: their 
money. While current clients can bring you three things: their money, 
referrals, and more money.  
The math leads you to the best and most cost -effective way to generate 
additional revenue. Have a plan in place to ensure your clients are advocates 
of your The DRIPBaR location.

Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                             Sales  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page G -17 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Membership Pricing  
A membership offers a once - or twice -a-month drip option along with 
monthly recurring benefits. Membership can help lower costs for members. 
See the examples of membership offerings below.  
Maintain has one Lifestyle Drip per month , in addition to:  
‚Ä¢ All additional drips and services are an extra 20% off  
‚Ä¢ Exclusive monthly member perk  
‚Ä¢ Free drink with each drip  
‚Ä¢ Four Wellness Credits per month for additional services (Th ese will 
vary per store offerings, but may include Red  Light, Compression, 
HALO Therapy, Infrared Sauna, or B12 shots)  
Improve has two Lifestyle Drips per month , in addition to:  
‚Ä¢ All additional drips and services are an extra 25% off  
‚Ä¢ Exclusive monthly member perk  
‚Ä¢ Free drink with each drip  
‚Ä¢ Six Wellness Credits per month for additional services (Th ese will vary 
per store offerings, but may include Red  Light, Compression, HALO 
Therapy, Infrared Sauna, or B12 shots)  
The Founder 's Club is available during the POP phase until the Grand 
Opening. It offers exclusive benefits that end after the Grand Opening:  
‚Ä¢ 20% off any membership program  
‚Ä¢ Four free B12 shots in a 12 -month period  
‚Ä¢ Gift bag at their first appointment  
‚Ä¢ Entry into  raffle to win  over $150  
‚Ä¢ Monthly member perks  
‚Ä¢ Access to exclusive events  
Founder's Club = All is the same as Maintain and Improve except for the 
pricing difference for both Maintain and Improve.  
Memberships are billed monthly and can be cancel led at any time. Any 
unused drips can be used at another time.

Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                             Sales  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page G -18 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Eight Critical Steps for Membership Sales  
1. The Call:  As described previously, be attentive, ask about their goals, 
gather information, and make recommendations based on their goals 
and information about health status.  
2. The Greeting:  Engage new clients with, "Hello and welcome to The 
DRIPBaR. I 'm [name] and am happy to help with any questions you 
have. " Greet current clients with, "Hello [client name], nice to see you 
again. I have you scheduled for the [name of the drip] today. You 
usually like to add [add -on name] ; would you like to include that today 
as well? " 
3. Tour of the Location:  Show them exactly how your location meets their 
needs, demonstrating value and appreciation of their investment in 
their health journey. Show the standards of the lab to demonstrate 
how serious you are about client safety. Show the lounge to 
demonstrate t he comfort and relaxation of the med spa environment.  
4. Needs Analysis:  The needs analysis is critical to providing personalized 
solutions and value. Ask, "What made you come in today? " Find out 
what they need from a drip or what they are hoping to achieve.  
5. Discuss the Price:  Share options aligned with their goals. Offer one or 
two options that demonstrate you listened to their needs and 
illustrated the value. If appropriate, introduce how membership or a 
package can save money.  
6. Ask for the Sale:  Create a sense of urgency without being pushy. Make 
the potential client feel like the membership is specially made for 
them. Schedule their appointment before  they leave.  
7. Ask for Referrals:  Whether the person joins or not, ask for referrals, as 
referrals provide incentives for the client and leads for your The 
DRIPBaR.  
8. Overcome Objections:  Ask questions about their objections and offer 
solutions. Circle back and ask for the sale again.  
 
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                             Sales  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page G -19 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Packages  
In a similar fashion  as membership , you can rely on building your 
relationships with current clients and members to convert them into 
purchasing the packages you offer. The data you collect and the referrals 
you receive should be the majority of that growth. However, because 
packages focus  on specific areas to feel better and to have a healthier 
lifestyle, there is a real opportunity to grow this revenue stream by taking 
advantage of individual client knowledge of their motivation or "why" they 
seek your services. Highlighting  packages can be helpful in education and 
building the brand. Wh ile many think IV drips equal hydration, the promoted 
packages aid in introducing other benefits of IV Therapy.  
Packages are great for those who do not want to commit to a membership 
but appreciate savings on their frequent visits. Examples of packages 
include:  
‚Ä¢ Purchase three IV drips or IM Quick Shots, get 5% off. (Ideal for 
someone with the flu who wants a service every other day for a week 
to recover.)  
‚Ä¢ Purchase six IV drips or IM Quick Shots, get 10% off.  
‚Ä¢ Purchase 10 IV drips or IM Quick Shots, get 15% off. (Economical for 
those with active cancer coming in one to two times a week or those 
doing a heavy metal detox weekly.)  
Seek p roper alliances with medical providers and other potential partners to 
assist in highlighting certain packages. For instance, local cancer cent res and 
oncologists would be a great resource to connect with about the Health 
Support High Dose Vitamin C Package.  
A key benefit to spending more time, resources, and budget on promoting 
packages is that multiple visits help significantly with recurring revenue and 
the long -term value of a client.  
The goal of increasing recurring revenue through packages and 
memberships should be a part of every location 's strategy. Recurring  
monthly revenue means predictable income. Franchisees can more 
effectively project sales and services based on the member count and 
services mix.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                             Sales  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page G -20 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Group Sales  
Growing paid "on- and off -" premises events is a great way to provide an 
influx of revenue to your monthly balance sheet. Offering m any drips at one 
time for bachelorette, bachelor, or wedding parties, whether on -premises or 
through mobile services, can help spike your monthly revenue. Determining 
tactics that can support your group business and setting a monthly goal to 
ensure you are  putting the time and resources behind this initiative can 
make a slow month great, and a busy month spectacular.  
Sales Support  
We host a company -wide sales call every Friday at 12 p.m. EST. All Team 
Member s are invited to  attend the call and calls are recorded and posted to 
SharePoint for those who cannot attend. This call allows for Owners to share 
and gain ideas from peers and gauge what is working and what is not 
working across the company.  
We also offer one -on-one sales call options and two additional group calls. 
One of the calls is specifically for those locations still in pre  sale. Once a new 
location opens its doors, we aim to have weekly contact for at least four 
months.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Section H: Daily Operations  
Hours of Operation  
The Franchisee shall ensure that the franchised business remains open to 
the public and operational during the following minimum hours of operation:  
‚Ä¢ Monday through Friday: 10:00 a.m. to 7:00 p.m.  
‚Ä¢ Saturday: 10:00 a.m. to 6:00 p.m.  
‚Ä¢ Sunday: 10:00 a.m. to 4:00 p.m.  
The Franchisee may, at their discretion, operate the franchised business 
beyond these minimum hours without the necessity of obtaining the 
Franchisor‚Äôs consent. However, any request to operate the Franchised 
Business for fewer hours than those prescribed above must be submitted in 
writing to the Franchisor, accompanied by a detailed business case 
supporting the rationale for the proposed reduction in hours.  
The Franchisor retains sole and absolute discretion in approving or rejecting 
such requests and shall not be obligated to grant any such approval. The 
Franchisee shall not implement reduced hours of operation unless and until 
express written consent is pro vided by the Franchisor.  
Daily Operations: Front Desk Associate  
Preparing for the Day  
The Front Desk Associate holds a vital role at The DRIPBaR, often serving as 
the first point of contact for members and guests. This position helps to 
create a welcoming and professional atmosphere for everyone who enters 
the facility. Greeting members by name, providing information about The 
DRIPBaR's services and memberships, and handling check -in procedures to 
ensure only those clients with appointments are escorted to the lounge and 
handed off to the care of the Nursing staff are the primary responsibil ities of 
a Front Desk Associate.  
 
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                      Daily Operations  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page H -5 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Opening Duties  
With an orderly start to the day, the Team can adequately prepare, ensuring 
that systems are functioning and potential issues are addressed before they 
affect the client experience. This preparation creates a calm atmosphere 
throughout the day, which is co nducive to both effective teamwork and a 
relaxing environment for the clients.  
The Front Desk Associate, as key holder, arrives 15 -20 minutes prior to 
opening time. This allows for a walkthrough quality check and thorough daily 
planning. The Front Desk Associate conducts a brief quality check of the 
location each morning, which inclu des organiz ing, sanit izing, and ensuring 
the technology is working properly.  
The Opening Checklist includes the following tasks:  
‚Ä¢ Disarm the alarm.  
‚Ä¢ Clock in.  
‚Ä¢ Turn lights, fan, and hood on.  
‚Ä¢ Complete the temperature log for lab temperature and humidity as 
well as the refrigerator temperature.  
‚Ä¢ Set up the hood with disinfectant.  
‚Ä¢ Clean the horizontal surfaces.  
‚Ä¢ Open the door promptly at opening time.  
‚Ä¢ On Fridays, check the inventory.  
Once the opening tasks are completed, the Front Desk Associate reviews the 
day's schedule and appointments. They will review the drips scheduled for 
that day and ensure there is adequate staffing and supplies for each 
individual drip. It is especially important to pay attention to the first drip of 
the day and begin prepping for that  first client 's arrival.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                      Daily Operations  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page H -6 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Below is an example of a daily drip schedule (always highlight the first client 
in green):  
Before the location opens for the day, the Team will participate in a brief 
morning huddle. This meeting ensures each Team Member is familiar with 
the day 's schedule and subsequent expectations. The Nurses are assigned 
their drips for the day. The Nurses will also be provided with relevant 
background information on each client to ensure a personalized client 
experience.  
Closing Duties  
Organizing the location for the next day is an essential step that sets a 
positive tone and ensures a smooth workflow right from the start upon 
opening the next workday. With everything in its place, the Team can focus 
on providing client care without the stress of tidying up or searching for 
supplies. Being organized minimizes wait times for appointments and 
maximizes client satisfaction.  
The Nurse completes these tasks an hour before closing:  
1. Empty the hood.  
2. Clean open vials and containers with 70% isopropyl alcohol wipes and 
put them in the refrigerator.  
3. Clean the hood.  
4. Turn the hood and hood light off.  
5. Complete the temperature log.  
6. Complete the hood log.  Appointments Today: ( First thing Morning Setup)  
Order by time of appointment:  
1. Luke Skywalker (Improve Member): Powerpack + Taurine  
2. George Lucas (Repeat Client) : Allstar + VitC + GSH  
3. Boba Fett (Maintain Member): Time Machine + GSH  
4. Ben Kenobi (Package Holder): IM Supercharged 3 -pack 
5. Mos Eisley (1st Drip Client) : Soother + GSH + Arginine

How to Manage Angry Clients Using the LAST Model  
Our training program focuses on active listening to ensure Team Members 
provide undivided attention to clients. This will create a positive client 
experience and help prevent mix -ups in appointment times and service 
requests. Team Members also handle any i nitial complaints or issues that 
arise. They solve problems independently and creatively, which heads off 
client frustration . 
But, despite the Team 's best efforts, a client may occasionally become 
angry. The ability to manage angry clients effectively is a critical skill for 
professionals involved in customer service. The LAST model provides a 
straightforward framework for handling difficult situation s and ultimately 
turning them into positive client experiences. LAST stands for Listen, 
Apologize, Solve, and Thank. Here is a step -by-step guide on how to 
manage angry clients using the LAST model.  
1. Listen:  
a. It is essential to remain composed when addressing an irate 
client. Keep your tone of voice neutral, maintain eye contact, 
and focus on understanding the problem.  
b. Give the client space to express their frustration without 
interruption. This helps them feel heard and acknowledged.  
c. Demonstrate genuine concern for the client's issue by using 
phrases like "I understand how you feel," or, "That must have 
been frustrating."  
d. Ask clarifying questions: To ensure you understand the root 
cause of their concern, ask open -ended questions like, "Can you 
tell me more about what happened?" Or, "What would you like 
us to do about it?"  
e. Apologize: A sincere apology can go a long way in diffusing 
tension and addressing an unhappy client's emotional needs. 
Ensure your apology is genuine and does not appear scripted.  
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                      Daily Operations  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page H -12 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  2. Solve:  
a. To resolve the problem, o ffer practical steps based on the client's 
needs and preferences.  
b. Aim to surpass what the client expects by going the extra mile 
and offering additional help or support.  
c. If resolving the issue takes time, establish open lines of 
communication and keep clients updated regarding progress or 
delays.  
3. Thank:  
a. Extend gratitude to the client for bringing the issue to your 
attention, enabling your organization to learn and improve.  
b. Assure the client that their loyalty is valuable and remind them 
of your commitment to address any potential future concerns.  
Using the LAST model as a framework for managing angry clients can help 
build stronger relationships and ensure positive outcomes.  
Overall, the Front Desk Associate role requires excellent customer service 
skills, a friendly demeanor, and the ability to multitask in a fast -paced 
environment. Being attentive and responsive to members ' needs helps 
facilitate a positive experience and can significantly contribute to member 
retention.

Daily Operations: Nursing  
A strong Nursing staff is integral to a The DRIPBaR location 's success. A 
location 's Nursing staff has a wide variety of responsibilities; these include 
managing the lounge and lab, administering the IV therapies and IM Quick 
Shots to clients, and maintaining the lab 's sanitation.  
Nurses ' shifts are typically 9 a.m. to 6 p.m. Nurses are highly encouraged to 
arrive 15 minutes before the start of their shift, in order to adequately set up 
the lab and prepare for the first clients of the day.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                      Daily Operations  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page H -14 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Operating the Lab  by Nursing  
As stated above, a location 's Nursing staff has a wide variety of 
responsibilities which include managing the lounge, catering to clients, and 
running the lab. Nurses ' shifts are typically 9 a.m. to 6 p.m.  
When Nurses arrive for their shift, they will need to enter a code in order to 
gain access to the lab. Once they are in the lab, their first priorities are 
hygiene and sanitation. Nurses are required to safely pull back their hair and 
complete the appropriate handwashing procedure. After this, the Nurse must 
clean the hood and insulator. It is important to clean the hood consistently 
throughout the day.  
Once these tasks are completed, the Nurse activates the hood and allows it 
to run and cycle. The Nurse should check the daily appointment schedule to 
determine the necessary drips and subsequent timing.  
When opening/closing the lab, the Nurse is responsible for sanitizing the lab. 
The hood, floors, and surfaces must be thoroughly cleaned and documented 
in the Cleaning Log.  
Per 797 requirements, a monthly surface test is required to check for fungus 
and bacteria within the hood. The Nurse is required to swab multiple 
surfaces and send in the samples, mailing them out to the designated lab. 
Test results will be returned to the  front desk.  
Initial Lab Set up 
At eight weeks prior to opening, the lab is fully and properly set up 
according to the approved Lasky plan and compliance set forth by the 
Medical Team. To get there, we provide you with some directions for setup, 
examples of current DRIPBaR labs, and opti ons to guide you in the lab setup 
process. After completing the setup, you then upload photos to the 
document checklist for review to ensure compliance with the Brand 
Standards.

Inventory Management  
Initial Orders  
The list of initial products to order will be sent to you by the Pharmacy 
Team. It will contain the products and quantities to reflect what you will 
need for your Friends and Family Event and your first weeks open.  
Orders will arrive in 24 -72 hours, except for supply chain issues, which we 
will help you navigate as they arise.  
Open shipments as soon as they arrive and check off the products as they 
arrive.  
IV Vitamins/Medications  
All The DRIPBaR products are sourced from 503B -accredited compounding 
pharmacies. Whenever possible, the products come as multi -dose vials 
(MDV).  
Some products come as single -dose vials (SDV) and should NOT be used for 
multiple doses.  
503A products are client -specific and are not included in the initial order.  
Medical Supplies  
All locations will be able to order all supplies and vitamins from one place, 
called "The DRIPBaR Pharmacy. " 
This one -stop shop allows products to be sourced from multiple vendors (Ex: 
McKesson, Medline, Empower, Olympia Pharmacy, etc.) and offered in one 
place. This one -shop process allows The DRIPBaR Pharmacy Team to vet and 
approve vendors, which ensures  control over quality and products, as well as 
much more competitive pricing.  
Why is consistency crucial for The DRIPBaR supply chain?  
‚Ä¢ Our franchise is in a growth mode ‚Äî we are adding new cent res 
monthly. It is important to order all medical supplies and equipment in 
the same way to identify opportunities and standardize products.

Lot and Expiration Date Protocol  
The lot number is an identification number assigned to a quantity or lot of 
material from a single manufacturer. Lot numbers can typically be found on 
the outside of the packaging.  
Lot tracking is an effective method through which pharmaceutical 
manufacturers can track and trace their medication. This allows healthcare 
companies to remove both counterfeit medications and recalled medications. 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                      Daily Operations  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page H -22 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Lot tracking is essential for inventory management and supply chain 
integrity. Lot tracking records data on a specific quantity of product ‚Äî 
gallons, pounds, etc. ‚Äî and makes it easy for manufacturers to trace the 
raw materials within a specific batch of m edications.  
Lot tracking simplifies the process of determining:  
‚Ä¢ Which batches of medication are ready for purchase?  
‚Ä¢ Which batches are expired?  
‚Ä¢ Which batches of medication need to be recalled?  
(In the event of a recall, lot tracking allows the manufacturer to easily 
identify and target the specific problematic batch.)  
To make this possible, each batch created is assigned a lot code, which is a 
unique series of numbers specific to that batch. In the event of a recall, 
manufacturers can use lot codes to see when the problem happened and 
which products were affected.  
Lot codes can also be used to answer client , government, or processing 
questions and create the Pedigrees and ePedigrees required by law. These 
Pedigrees are identifying statements provided by certain wholesale 
distributors "prior to each wholesale distribution of prescription drugs. " 
The expiration date is the final day that the manufacturer guarantees the full 
potency and safety of a  medication or product . 
Our Lot and Expiration Spreadsheet:  
1. Whenever a new product comes in, ALWAYS record it in this 
spreadsheet. This is part of your Pharmacy Log.  
2. The sheet has many tabs along the bottom to keep track of each IV 
vitamin individually. Make sure to fill it in completely.  
3. Trends: Over the next year, you will be able to notice trends, and this 
will make ordering easier. You will also be able to see if you over -
ordered any product by including expired items.  
4. These lots and expiration dates will be used if there is ever a recall.

Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                      Daily Operations  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page H -24 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  All infusions are supported by research -based evidence in cellular biology, 
animal studies, or in  some cases, research on human subjects. All infusions 
at The  DRIPBaR  are backed by published scientific and medical articles. This 
is important to emphasize t o your clients, as it leads to credibility and the 
client's confidence in  treatment.  
Unlike Health Canada (HC) approved drugs, health support infusions are not 
intended to treat disease,  therefore, they do not require "proof" in order to 
justify value. We describe the infusions as "evidence -informed and 
scientifically supported." In addition to the external research that we have 
accumulated, the goal of The DRIPBaR Research and  Development Team is 
to understand and analyze the results of infusions for clien ts served by  The 
DRIPBaR.  
Research articles are located on SharePoint . See the articles listed in an 
Excel document. At the bottom of the Excel document, you can scroll 
through to see all IV drips. IV ingredient lists may look the same for some 
drips, but the amounts may  vary greatly for each infusion. Please refer to 
the IV drip stickers or IV drip menu for exact amounts. The IV ingredient list 
is proprietary and confidential.  
While the research is important, clients often want to know why they should 
use IV Therapy. The simple explanation is there is no better way to achieve 
high-dose vitamins and deliver them directly to the cells than via  direct 
infusion. Many people are afflicted with conditions  that can impair the 
absorption of vitamins, like irritable bow el disorder or  leaky gut; even the 
use of  antacids, antibiotics, and  Nexium or Prilosec  may interfere with 
nutrient  absorption.  
Vitamin insufficiency can lead to an array of symptoms  
that include  depressed mood,  increased anxiety, fatigue, muscle  aches, 
neuropathy, brain fog, and other symptoms  that compromise quality of life.  
Many of these symptoms overlap a host  of other diagnosed  conditions, and 
because nutrition and vitamin support tend to be under -discussed, the 
true cause may often be  overlooked.  
The DRIPBaR  clients have chosen to use IV vitamin support  to help them 
with afflictions ranging from  common  colds, headaches,  pain, or any of the 
conditions listed  above. Other clients without any conditions use infusions  of 
vitamins as a part of their hea lth maintenance routine.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Complementary Care  
The treatments offered at The  DRIPBaR  are intended to  improve the  client's 
quality of life, while possibly slowing  the rate of cancer  progression, or 
decreasing the chance of  cancer recurrence.  
The treatment modalities that we recommend are based  upon the  scientific 
evidence regarding laboratory evidence  of toxicity toward  cancer, individual 
case reports of  benefit, and the accumulated decades of  clinical 
experience  by other clinicians providing similar treatments.  
Our recommendations are also supported by the low rate of  adverse  effects 
regarding complementary treatment. Complementary care refers to any 
cancer treatment outside conventional medicine. Complementary care 
treatments are believed to help  in the fight ag ainst cancer even though they 
are not HC-approved.  
In the realm of complementary cancer care, nothing has  been shown to be 
more effective than intravenous  infusions of high -dose vitamin C (IVC) and 
alpha  lipoic acid (ALA). These treatments have been around for decades 
and have laboratory evidence of  effect iveness against  cancer cells. There are 
also years of case studies of individuals who responded to these 
complementary agents.  
Despite many decades of use and thousands of clinical  cases, the use of 
these  products has not been proven to  cure cancer in double -blind, placebo -
controlled  studies.  
Client Information  
Clients are informed that intravenous vitamin C has been used for many 
decades  to help fight cancer.  Unlike oral vitamin C,  which is a  powerful 
antioxidant, intravenous vitamin C is a cancer -killing  pro-oxidant.  
It leads to the  development of  hydrogen peroxide  in the area of  the cells. 
This substance is toxic to cancer cells, but  harmless to the  natural cells of 
your body.  
In addition to attacking cancer cells by producing  hydrogen peroxide, 
vitamin C also is felt to enhance  the amount of collagen formed throughout 
the body,  thereby creating barriers that make it harder for  cancer to 
metastasize.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                      Daily Operations  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page H -27 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Vitamin C is extraordinarily safe.  Serious  complications  are rare. Once the 
infusion is started, it will  take anywhere from 30 to 60 minutes to be 
completed.  
As the infusion is taking place, clients  may feel mild nausea  or dizziness. The 
symptoms are the result of  lowering  blood sugar. When blood sugar is 
lowered, vitamin C  gains better access to the cancer cells,  enhancing 
its ability to do damage. The client may tolerate some minor  discomfort . 
However,  significant discomfort  can be  managed easily by slowing the rate 
of the infusion or  having something to eat.  
Remind the client  to: 
‚Ä¢ Arrive for their infusion well -hydrated and  having had something to 
eat.  
‚Ä¢ Eat a low -glycemic meal prior to  and post their  infusion .  
‚Ä¢ Not to take any antioxidant  supplements  on the day of their infusion.  
It should be emphasized that none of The DRIPBaR treatments are HC-
approved  for the treatment of cancer. Definitive proof of benefit is 
determined by  double -blind placebo -controlled studies and those have not 
been established at this  time. 
It should also be emphasized that we encourage clients to  continue  seeing 
their orthodox cancer specialist and  following their  recommendations for 
orthodox treatment.  
New Client Protocol  
Per provincial  and national IV industry regulations, it is required that a 
relationship be formed between the client and the location 's Medical 
Professional. Through a good faith exam, the client 's treatment plan will be 
established. A follow -up exam should occur every six months.  
Registered Nurses play a crucial role in the initial stages of client history 
taking. Their responsibilities include conducting comprehensive assessments 
to obtain a detailed medical history and understand each client's unique 
needs.  
This data collection is fundamental in determining the suitability and safety 
of IV Therapy for every individual. By asking pertinent questions about past 
and present health concerns, allergies, medication use, and specific fitness 
goals, Nurses ensure that IV treatments are tailored effectively to support 
the client's overall well -being.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                      Daily Operations  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page H -28 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Ongoing care by the Nurses includes monitoring clients' responses to the 
therapy, adjusting care plans accordingly, and providing education on 
maintaining optimal health benefits from the program. As trusted healthcare 
professionals, Nurses bridge critical communication b etween clients and the 
Medical Director, advocating for client safety and ensuring high -quality care 
throughout their journey.  
Preparing for Client Appointments  
Once the client finishes check -in at the front desk, they are handed off to 
the Nurse. We provide snacks and beverages and highly encourage the client 
to eat and drink before their drip. Blankets are also available to clients.  
Once the client is comfortable, the Nurse will check their vital signs. Once it 
is confirmed that their vitals are stable, the Nurse will begin the drip 
process. Throughout the drip process, it is important for the Nurse to check 
in on the client and ensur e their IV is flowing properly.  
If appropriate, the Nurse can inform the client of additional services such as 
the infrared sauna and red light room. Once their drip is finished, the client 
will be required to remain in the location for 15 minutes to make sure they 
do not have a negative  reaction.  
Next, the  Nurse hands off the client to the Front Desk Associate who will 
complete the check -out process with the client. Post -drip vital signs will be 
taken and once it is confirmed that they are stable, the client is able to leave 
the location.  
Nurses will receive a client approximately every 15 minutes. In between 
clients, Nurses can clean/sanitize, watch webinars, and review protocols. It 
is important for Nurses to always stay up to date and refresh their 
knowledge.  
In addition to scheduled individual clients, we also accept walk -ins, pairs, 
and groups. If an unanticipated group walks in, it is important for the whole 
Team to support the Nurse. The Front Desk Associate, Owner, and even an 
off-duty Nurse may be notifie d to assist , if need be.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Nurses' Role in Sales Process  
Nurses influence the sales of IV treatments and related services. By ensuring 
exceptional client care and education, Nurses foster trust and client 
satisfaction, increasing the likelihood of return visits and positive referrals. 
They do this by:  
‚Ä¢ Discussing the drips the client is receiving and their benefits.  
‚Ä¢ Suggesting that the client continue to improve their healthy lifestyle 
with regular drips or membership packages.  
‚Ä¢ Recommending the clients add supplements for continued 
maintenance.  
‚Ä¢ Remember that you literally have a captive audience, and you are the 
residential expert!

appointments, including the client 's names and the IV bags and IM Quick 
Shots to be prepared.  
Since the Nurse participates in the sales process, the daily sales update is 
included.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Who Can Mix and Administer IVs or IM Shots?  
As of July 2020, any Registered Nurse, Pharmacist, or Physician  can Mix and 
Administer IVs or IM Shots  if they have completed the following training s: 
‚Ä¢ Initial Fingertip Testing  (Must remain up to date on Testing After the 
Initial Test)  
‚Ä¢ The DRIPBaR University Training Program   
Note that requirements are province -specific; determine the requirements 
for the province  in which the franchised business is located.  
The following  Team Members  can start an IV:  
‚Ä¢ Registered Nurse  
‚Ä¢ Nurse Practitioner  
‚Ä¢ Physician 's Assistant  
‚Ä¢ Physician  
The following Team Members are allowed to administer an IM shot:  
‚Ä¢ Registered Nurse  
‚Ä¢ Nurse Practitioner  
‚Ä¢ Physician 's Assistant  
‚Ä¢ Physician  
‚Ä¢ Medical Assistant  
Anxious and Unwell Clients  
If a client expresses feelings of anxiety or fear, make sure to validate their 
concerns and respond in a compassionate manner. It is also encouraged to 
move them to a more private station to lessen their anxiety. It is also 
important to take their vital signs and ensure that they are stable enough to 
receive a drip.  
If a client comes in and is showing symptoms of the flu, COVID, etc., the 
Front Desk Associate should catch this before the client heads back. It may 
be in their best interest to reschedule their appointment. If the client is only 
slightly sick, place them  in a private room, so as not to spread to others. 
They may be offered a mask and an emesis bag.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual                      Daily Operations  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page H -32 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Additionally, clients may not receive treatment if they are intoxicated or 
under the influence.  
Emergency Protocol  
The Registered Nurse stays with the client during the initiation of IV Therapy 
and then takes post -drip vital signs to monitor for adverse reactions.  
Each location is equipped with an emergency kit. This kit contains 
epinephrine and Benadryl. Every morning, the Nurse should ensure that the 
kit contains the necessary supplies and that nothing is expired. An 
automated external defibrillator (AED) machine should  also be available and 
displayed in a public space. The AED needs to be checked monthly.  
All clinical protocols can be found on SharePoint.  
Training  
The DRIPBaR Corporate  has developed a Mentoring Program for Nurses to:  
‚Ä¢ Create a promotional path for site Nurses and increase retention of 
staff for Owners.  
‚Ä¢ Set a standard training and growth path for the Drip Specialists.  
‚Ä¢ Accelerate the rate of new location training.  
‚Ä¢ Expand the leaders within The DRIPBaR Research and 
Development/Medical Team.  
Tiers:  
 Level 1: Works at The DRIPBaR  
 Level 2: On site Lead 
 Level 3: Train the Trainer level  
All new Nurses begin at Level 1. After approximately six months of 
employment, a Nurse will be promoted to Level 2. Our highest -ranking 
Nurses, Level 3, are responsible for any Initial Training.  
See additional information about the Mentoring Program described in Section 
E Human Resources.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Section I: Business Management  
The DRIPBaR Revenue Streams  
Understanding data and information about clients and the pathway to 
revenue is crucial to maintaining and growing your business. There are four 
key revenue streams that, as a The DRIPBaR Owner, you must keep top of 
mind:  
‚Ä¢ Individual clients (new clients and existing clients)  
‚Ä¢ Memberships  
‚Ä¢ Packages  
‚Ä¢ Group sales (on -premises and off -premises mobile events)  
Each of these four revenue streams comes with varying needs and 
preferences from clients. Understanding the client's needs is crucial to know 
where they fit, or can fit, to fill up one or many of these revenue buckets.  
The focus should be on the individual revenue streams and how to optimize 
the pathway into your The DRIPBaR; and once there, the focus will be on 
how to increase the lifetime value (LTV) of a client during their The DRIPBaR 
journey.  
Having k nowledge of these pathways to revenue will allow you to devise 
precise tactics to maximize each revenue stream's potential. The way many 
Franchisees view marketing is with a pure tactical approach, with a focus on 
the tactic, rather than on the goal of the  tactic and the results sought after. 
That methodology is inverted and will underperform, leading to less impact 
on your budget and ultimately lower revenue.  
Build your local marketing plan with your goals in mind. Generating more 
revenue is not a goal ‚Äî it is an outcome that is too broad to build a proper 
marketing strategy. Only focusing on one or two tactics will lead you to 
underperform in revenue.  
A very pertinent example relates to SEO, SEM, and digital marketing in 
general. While these tactics are an important piece of your marketing mix, 
especially during launch and while you are initially building your brand, 
eventually they should only account for 10 -15% of your overall revenue; 
meaning you are focused on a fraction of the potential revenue if that is 
where you are spending most of your time and revenue.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual              Business Management  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page I -4 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Goal Analysis  
 
Owners can analyze their sales funnel's actual numbers at each stage ‚Äî 
right from lead acquisition to membership conversion and membership 
attrition. By examining the conversion rates of leads to appointments, they 
can identify bottlenecks in initial client engagement.  
Remember, marketing activities represent leads in the sales funnel. So, 
there are opportunities to adjust the upcoming marketing activities 
according to the mix and goals in line 3.  
With this data -focused approach, Owners pinpoint specific areas for 
operational improvement, marketing strategy enhancement, and service 
improvement toward optimizing their revenue streams.  
Controlling Costs  
Cost Per Acquisition  
While your local marketing activities generate leads that convert into 
memberships and additional revenue, controlling costs is vital for 
profitability. One critical component of cost control is the effective 
management of acquisition expenses. These are the funds spent on activities 
designed to attract new memb ers, such as advertising, promotional offers, 
and various forms of marketing.  
During the early going, you will have to rely on building the brand through 
events, grassroots marketing, advertising, and other tactics to introduce the 
prospect. As the months go by, asking these clients for referrals should be 
an intricate part of your strategy, as the referral comes at a lower price and 
is most likely to close.  
 


DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual              Business Management  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page I -5 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  With the  goal of the lowest possible CPA (cost per acquisition) , take your 
first set of clients, for whom you probably paid more to acquire, and utilize 
them to make introductions to get your next set of clients. This is a smart 
way to proceed toward achieving that lower CPA goal. Referral programs can  
require  more work and you will need to be proactive in your daily routine. 
However, referrals dramatically reduce the CPA of a client. You should have 
goals for a specific number of Referral Requests each mon th to bring the 
blended CPA of the totality of your active clients to a lower number.  
So, a careful balance must be struck. It is essential that these expenditures 
are sufficient to draw in new members consistently, yet be mindful not to 
exceed a certain threshold. By keeping the CPA lower than the lifetime value 
(LTV) of a member, a company can secure a healthy return on its 
investment, avoiding situations where marketing expenses eclipse the 
revenue generated by new member s. 
Operating Costs  
Operating costs represent another pivotal area for cost control. These 
include everyday expenses that keep the business running, such as utility 
fees, rent, employee wages, and any costs associated with delivering 
services to members. To mitigate these cos ts without sacrificing quality, 
follow The DRIPBaR System for operations and manage the labor costs. 
Initially, you will have the Nurse and the Front Desk Team Member. Add 
staff as membership increases and the Nurse 's time for client services, 
upsells, and education is maximized.  
Remember to r egular ly evaluat e membership fees . The DRIPBaR 
membership pricing caters to different clients' needs while encouraging 
upgrades. A review of the tiers with Corporate  ensures that prices charged 
to members are in line with market demand and are proportionate to the 
costs incurred by the business for providing its services. Adjusting these 
models as needed can help maintain competitiveness and profitability.  
Encourage membership upgrades through marketing and sales efforts. You 
can incentivize purchases of higher -value plans and increase overall revenue 
without significantly impacting service delivery costs.  
 
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual              Business Management  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page I -6 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Member Retention  
Focusing on current members usually proves more cost -effective than 
acquiring new ones, since existing customer bases already understand and 
value your service. Engagement initiatives such as personalized 
communication, exclusive services, and seeking dire ct feedback can deepen 
client relationships without incurring high costs.  
Monitor Other Key Performance Indicators  
Monitor other key performance metrics including the percentage of clients 
who stop using the service over a given period, as well as the LTV which 
predicts the net profit attributed to an entire future relationship with a client. 
These data points serve as  indicators of financial performance and help 
business leaders make strategic decisions about where to reduce spending 
or where to invest more heavily for better returns.  
Risk Management  
To maximize profits and ensure your business 's stability, you will need to 
properly manage your liability risks. Risks include those associated with 
safety and product safety. Here are minimal guidelines:  
‚Ä¢ Follow all federal, provincial , and local employment -related laws.  
‚Ä¢ Follow all provincial  and local regulations for safety and sanitation 
conscientiously.  
‚Ä¢ Comply with  PIPEDA  standards for privacy ( https://laws -
lois.justice.gc.ca/eng/acts/p -8.6/). 
‚Ä¢ Comply with 797 standards.  
‚Ä¢ Maintain the equipment and facility daily to avoid injury or illness. 
Remove any hazards.  
‚Ä¢ Follow business practices that reduce your risk of legal exposure. Upon 
signing your Franchise Agreement, work with an attorney to set up a 
corporation and shield your business assets from liability.  
‚Ä¢ Ensure all employees, including management, are aware of The 
DRIPBaR safety and service standards and protocols, as well as any 
regulatory requirements.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual              Business Management  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page I -7 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Insurance Requirements  
Business liability insurance is indispensable as a safeguard against potential 
legal claims arising from unforeseen circumstances, ensuring that the 
franchised business can continue to offer its services without the crippling 
financial repercussions of lit igation. The Franchisee must obtain the 
minimum required insurance coverage 30 days prior to opening the 
franchised operations or upon signing the lease agreement, whichever 
comes first. Because of the ever -changing business practices faced in the IV 
Therapy industry, Corporate  may, in its sole and absolute discretion, modify 
the types and amounts of coverage required.  
Inventory Control  
Inventories help ensure your location has an accurate record of supplies 
available for use. Due to the large volume of materials used daily in 
preparation, it is important to adhere to inventory procedures so that you 
maintain appropriate levels of supplie s. Keep in mind that maintaining too 
much inventory causes high expenditures, impacts cash flow, and 
contributes to waste due to expiration.  
Monitoring inventories also provides a safeguard against losses caused by 
waste, theft, and abuses of employee privileges. It can be challenging to get 
your employees to accurately count an inventory. The frequency and items 
inventoried depend on the indiv idual location 's experience with accuracy and 
losses in net revenue. If the cost of goods (COGS) sold is unusually high, 
taking an inventory may spot the issues so you can plan strategies to reduce 
the COGS.  
Business Continuity Plan  
When a catastrophic or unexpected event occurs, your business must protect 
employees and, to the extent possible, continue regular operations. A 
Business Continuity Plan details the steps you will follow to continue 
operating despite a natural or man -made disaster ‚Äî or a pandemic.  
Business Continuity Planning focuses on multiple aspects of your business 
with the goal of helping you make sure you can access the people, 
processes, and technology you need to operate after a disruption in normal 
operations.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual              Business Management  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page I -8 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Create a Business Continuity Plan  
To make sure you have a solid plan in place ‚Äî before you need it ‚Äî 
examine key areas and how you will address them. These include:  
‚Ä¢ Critical processes, operations, and other vital aspects of your business.  
‚Ä¢ Employee responsibilities and designated backup personnel for 
essential functions, including management.  
‚Ä¢ Available facilities, utilities, computers, and staff ‚Äî and whether these 
will meet your business 's needs.  
‚Ä¢ A designated recovery site for employees to resume work and a plan 
for communications, data connectivity, desktops, and workspaces at 
that site.  
‚Ä¢ Processes to continue your business 's financial functions, including 
payroll, rent, and vendor payments, etc.  
‚Ä¢ Communication with employees, clients, and your community.  
‚Ä¢ Strategy to share disaster preparedness plans and find opportunities 
for cooperation within your community.  
Financial Help During a Business Interruption  
If conditions require you to cease your business 's operations, consider these 
options for financial support:   
1.  Explore your business interruption insurance coverage; contact your 
agent for guidance.  
2.  Check loan and grant options available from the Canada Small 
Business Financing Loan (CSBFL) . Apply immediately in case funds are 
limited and dispersed on a "first come, first served " basis.  
3.  Explore relief or loans from your municipality, province , or local 
economic development cent res. Again, apply immediately if funds are 
limited.  
4.  Check trade associations, foundations, and other organizations for 
grants, loan opportunities, and available resources.
