Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Opening Hood and Employee Testing Procedure  
 Hood Install  30 Days Before Friends and Family Event  
1 Hood Certification  Call and schedule your inspection four weeks before your 
Friends and Family Event. This inspection will look at the 
mechanical parts of the hood such as airflow, HEPA  filter, seals, 
and vents. It takes  approximately five days for the report.  
2 Environmental Testing  To ensure there is no bacteria and fungi present, take air and 
surface sampling from various spots inside your hood. Report 
back in 14 days.  
3 Media Fill Testing 
(Employee)  Perform an aseptic manufacturing procedure using a sterile 
microbiological growth medium, in place of the drug solution, to 
test whether the aseptic procedures are adequate to prevent 
contamination during actual drug production. Report back in 14 
days.  
4 Gloved Fingertip Testing 
(Employee)  Monitor bacterial growth. Fingertip testing determines the 
efficiency of cleaning programs and hand washing  techniques by 
monitoring the growth of bacterial colonies on incubated 
samples. Report back in 14 days.  
5 Hand Hygiene and Garbing  This will be completed by a Corporate  Team Member at your 
onsite training.  
6 Requirements  All tests with a passing score need to be completed before the 
hood can be used for mixing. At your Friends and Family Event, 
we need to be able to use your hood for training purposes.  
FAQS:  
How do I get this completed?  Our vendor , HEPA , will do Hood, Environmental 
Testing, Media Tip Testing , and Gloved Fingertip 
Testing. You will contact HEPA to do the testing.  
How often do I need to do Hood Testing?  Hood certification is every six months, completed 
by HEPA . 
How often do I need my employees to do Media 
Fill, Gloved Fingertip Testing, and Hand Hygiene 
and Garbing?  Initial testing is upon hiring for anyone who is 
going to be compounding  in the hood. It is then 
required every six months for all locations.  
What do I tell the company when I call for 
certification and testing?  Tell the certifier which hood model you have and 
that you need certification and testing USP 797 
guidelines.  
What testing do I need?  See numbers 1 -4, above.  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual      Sanitizing and Maintenance  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page K -8 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Beyond -Use Date  
Compounding Sterile Preparations (CSPs)  have a limited  shelf life. There is 
always a  risk of microbial  contamination in CSPs.  There is more risk 
for contamination to  CSPs if the minimum practices  required in  the USP 797 
quality system are not  followed.  Every CSP that you compound  must be 
prepared using  an aseptic technique  and assigned an appropriate beyond -
use date.  
According to USP 797, a beyond -use date is "the date  or the hour and date, 
beyond which the preparation  must not be used and must be discarded." 
The BUD  is determined from the date and time that preparation  of the CSP is 
started  and alerts the staff of the  time that administration of a  CSP may not 
begin.  
After mixing an infusion or IM shot (if mixed in the  hood):  
‚Ä¢ Can keep for up to 12 hours at room temperature or up to 24 hours 
refrigerated.  
‚Ä¢ All mobile menu drips mixed outside of the  sterile hood must  be used 
within one hour of  mixing.  
‚Ä¢ SUV (Single -Use Vial): Any single -use vial punctured  is good for four 
hours and then needs to be  discarded (or as noted per manufacturer).  
o For amino acids , treat as single -use due to potential for bacterial 
growth. Discard  after use.  
‚Ä¢ MDV (Multi -dose Vial): Once punctured, they can be  used for 28 days. 
They must be stored per the manufacturer's recommendation when 
not in  use. Vials must be labeled with the date that they will expire.  
‚Ä¢ Ampoules: Ampoules are single -dose vials and need to  be 
used immediately. Any unused product needs to  be discarded.  
Beyond -Use Date Versus Expiration Date  
Beyond -Use Date:  Either the date or the end date, after which the CSP must 
not be used. It is determined from the date and time that compounding 
began. Determining a BUD  is based on chemical stability and microbial 
stability.  
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual      Sanitizing and Maintenance  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page K -9 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Expiration Date:  The time during which a product can be expected to  meet 
the requirements of the compendium monograph, if one exists;  or maintain 
the expected quality, provided it is kept under specific  storage conditions.  
The environment where a CSP is compounded significantly impacts the 
sterility assurance of the CSP.  
Compounding location is now a major factor in determining the BUD that can 
be assigned to the CSP.  
USP 797 (2019) has two compounding categories to which the BUD can be 
assigned. It is based on  whether the CSP is prepared in a Primary 
Engineering Control (PEC), in a Segregated Compounding  Area (SCA), or in 
a lab suite.  
Those prepared in an SCA are considered Category 1 and are assigned 
shorter dating than CSPs  prepared in a lab suite which are considered 
Category 2.  
At The  DRIPBaR  we use the  SCA and are considered Category 1.  
Temperature Controls  
BUD requirements differ based on the storage  temperature of the 
preparation. It is important  to know these temperature ranges , as these  are 
required in USP  797. 
‚Ä¢ Controlled room temperature 20 to 25¬∞C or 68  to 77¬∞F  
‚Ä¢ Controlled refrigerator 2 to 8¬∞C or 36 to 46¬∞F  
Temperatures in all areas where CSPs are  stored and compounded must be 
monitored  and documented daily (this is documented on the Lab Conditions 
Log found on FranConnect).  
How to Maintain USP 797 Compliance  
Designated to protect clients and staff, USP 797 requires  attention to three 
main areas to ensure compliance:  
‚Ä¢ Staff training and  ongoing guidance  
‚Ä¢ Determination of categories  
‚Ä¢ Development and  implementation of appropriate policies and 
procedures  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual      Sanitizing and Maintenance  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page K -10 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Staff Training  
USP 797 applies to everyone involved in sterile compounding: pharmacists, 
nurses, physicians, and pharmacy technicians. At The DRIPBaR, USP 797 
applies primarily to Nurses.  Staff USP 797 training  should cover best 
practices and core competencies for each t ype of  employee, ideally in a 
hands -on, situation -based learning formation with  both practical and written 
exams.  
Category Determination  
In 2008, USP designated three levels of risk as it relates to compounded 
pharmaceuticals  (low, medium, and high).  Now the chapter focuses 
on where  the compounded preparation is being made, making the 
lines completely clear and eliminating frustration when trying to 
achieve  compliance. Low Risk is mixing only one item in the bag of fluid.  
The DRIPBaR  locations are considered Medium Risk.  
Policies and Procedures  
To comply with USP 797, there are policies and procedures that 
cover  specific situations that arise during compounding. Templates and 
reference  resources make the development of these policies and procedures 
easier and  help ensure that staff know what to do and how to document 
their actions.  
These can be found on SharePoint.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Hood Training  
A laminar flow hood's purpose is  to create a clean, contaminant -free 
workspace by providing a steady, unidirectional flow of HEPA -filtered air over 
the work surface, protecting sensitive materials like biological samples or 
electronic components from airbo rne particles and contamination during 
manipulation;  essentially, it allows for precise work with delicate items 
without introducing unwanted particles from the surrounding environment.  
Pharmacy Isolators:  
‚Ä¢ Compounding Aseptic Isolators (CAI) are primary engineering 
controls  designed to  meet the needs of the USP 797 standards for the 
compounding  pharmacy.  
‚Ä¢ Create a positive pressure, clean air (ISO Class 5) controlled 
environment  specifically for aseptic compounding of non -hazardous 
drugs. The  HEPA -filtered work area maintains a positive pressure 
relative to the  interchange  compartment, which operates at a p ositive 
air pressure relative to  the surrounding room. These two levels of 
protection minimize the possibility  of contamination migrating into the 
work zone.  
Hood Certification:  
‚Ä¢ Your hood needs to be inspected by a third party upon installation, 
then every six months. They will check the  HEPA filter, pressure 
gauges,  seal, and basically  everything else to make sure it is 
performing the way  it should  be. 
The hood is like a lab. The antechamber acts the same as the outer chamber 
of the hood.  
Environmental Testing  
Monthly testing includes the inner surfaces of your hood.  
Testing Company  
When the  company  come s to install and certify your hood, ask them if they 
can also perform the  Environmental Testing.  
Environmental Testing consists of air and surface sampling inside 
your hood and looks for bacteria, mold, fungus, and spores.  
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual      Sanitizing and Maintenance  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page K -14 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Ask for the  following  certification s of the company:  
‚Ä¢ CETA (Controlled Environmental Testing Association) Certification  
‚Ä¢ CNBT (Controlled National Board of Testing) Certification  
Print the certifications and put in the USP 797 Binder.  
DO NOT  use a company if they do not have t hese certification s. 
If the Department of Pharmacy comes in and inspects you, it is 
important  you use the highest standards of testing.  
Temperature and Humidity Log  
The conditions under which a  compounded  sterile preparation  (CSP) 
is stored play an important  role in determining the beyond -use date (BUD).  
Proper storage has been shown to slow  the growth of  microorganisms. 
This allows  for longer BUDs for CSPs  stored  under  colder temperatures 
versus  controlled  room temperature.  
Temperatures of the refrigerator  and room, as well as the  humidity 
level of the room, need to be documented  in your log in the morning  and at 
the end of  the day.  
Hood Sleeve Change Log  
Sleeves are changed every six  months.  Make sure  you purchase 
short sleeves.  
The log is taped in your lab and documented  monthly. Put  in USP 797 
Binder  yearly.  
Media Fill Challenge Test  
Media Fill Challenge Testing  is used to  verify  that personnel  have the 
necessary  skills to compound aseptic  preparations.  Your Registered Nurses 
will do this upon hire, then every 6 months. This can be done through 
Aerobiology/Pace Labs. Results take appro ximately 7 days to get back.  
Fingertip Testing  
The initial  Gloved Fingertip Sampling  is to include three separate pairs of 
sterile  gloves  put on in an aseptic manner  on three different occasions. The 
fingertips  and thumb of both hands  are to be  tested.  Two separate agar 
plates  (paddles are  not recommen ded) are to be  used; one  agar plate for 
each hand.

Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Objectives:  Gloved  Fingertip  Sampling  (GFS) is an integral part of 
ensuring  that pharmacy  personnel are  aware of  the microbiological 
bioburden  on their gloves  since touch  contamination  is believed to be the 
primary  source  of compounded sterile preparation  (CSP)  contamination  
Fundamentals  
‚Ä¢ Must have a Line of Demarcation in the lab ‚Äì blue painter's tape 
works.  
‚Ä¢ Non-sterile gloves must be on  at all times while in the lab,  and hair 
must be pulled back.  
‚Ä¢ Practi se excellent hand hygiene: short nails, non -painted.  
‚Ä¢ Follow proper mixing techniques.  
‚Ä¢ Clear solutions in one syringe.  
‚Ä¢ Coloured solutions in another syringe.  
‚Ä¢ Check on the client and site of IV no less than every 10 minutes.  
‚Ä¢ Trust your gut. If you are not 100% positive about something, double -
check.  
‚Ä¢ Cleaning requirements  are three types:  cleaning, disinfectant, 
sporicidal.  
Cleaning fundamentals:  
‚Ä¢ Cleaning Agent  
o An agent used for the removal of removal of residues (e.g., dirt, 
debris,  microbes, and residual drugs or chemicals) from 
surfaces.  
‚ñ™ Daily 
‚Ä¢ Disinfectant  
o A chemical or physical agent used on inanimate surfaces and 
objects to  destroy fungi, viruses, and bacteria.  
‚ñ™ Daily 
‚Ä¢ Sporicidal Agent  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC

Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page K -16 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  o A chemical or physical agent that destroys bacterial and fungal 
spores when  used at a sufficient concentration for a specified 
contact time. It is  expected to kill all vegetative microorganisms.  
‚ñ™ Monthly  
Line of Demarcation  
Design the facility so that there is a clear,  visible Line of Demarcation  in the 
antechamber area or  SCA that  separates  the dirty area from the clean area. 
The line  provides a  visual job aid to  assist  compounding personnel in 
properly  sequencing  the donnin g and  doffing of their 
personal  protective  equipment (PPE).

The DRIPBaR Hood Cleaning  
Morning Hood Cleaning  
Procedures:  
1. If the hood has remained closed and unused throughout the night, you 
may turn on the fan and light and let cycle for 10 minutes prior to 
mixing. You do not need to open the hood.  
2. Sanitize gloved hands with sterile 70% isopropyl alcohol solution 
(sIPA).  
3. Enter hood through sleeves, spray nonwoven wiper with sIPA to clean 
work surface and gloves before any compounding.  
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual      Sanitizing and Maintenance  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page K -17 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  Throughout the day, use a spray bottle filled with sterile 70% alcohol and 
low-particulate wipes inside the hood to wipe surfaces, vials, gloves, and 
supplies entering the antechamber. We also suggest you have sterile alcohol 
wipes in the antechamber to utilize on vial tops and IV bag injection ports.  
Evening Hood Cleaning  
Procedures:  
1. Prior to starting cleaning , perform hand hygiene and  full garb (gown, 
mask, hair cap, booties, and gloves).  
2. Sanitize gloved hands with a sterile 70% alcohol solution (IPA).  
3. After turning off the fan, open the front window of the hood by lifting 
the handles.  
4. Using disinfectant cleaner (see chart for approved disinfectants), first 
spray all hard surfaces ‚Äî DO NOT spray ceiling or sleeves/gloves. 
Allow the cleaner to sit for 10 minutes.  
5. Using low -particulate wipes, wipe each surface that was sprayed with 
disinfectant.  
6. Follow guidelines of working Top to Bottom and Back to Front. Use 
overlapping, linear strokes when cleaning.  
7. Ensure you use a new lint -free cloth for each chamber you clean. 
Change wipes if they become visibly soiled or begin shedding small 
particles.  
8. Surfaces to be cleaned:  
a. Back Wall (Main Chamber and Antechamber)  
b. Side Walls (Main Chamber and Antechamber)  
c. Work Surface (Main Chamber and Antechamber)  
d. Area under Work Surface ‚Äî lift Work Surface tray (Main 
Chamber and Antechamber)  
e. Glove Port Window  
f. Transfer Door (both sides, Main Chamber and Antechamber)  
 

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual      Sanitizing and Maintenance  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page K -18 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  9. Following cleaning with disinfectant, repeat steps 1 -6 with 
decontaminant (sterile 70% IPA) and lint -free cloths on all surfaces, 
including the sleeves/isolator gloves. Be sure to NEVER spray the 
ceiling of the isolator. Sterile IPA should always be the la st step in the 
hood cleaning process and may be used on gloves and sleeves.  
10. Close the hood, carefully ensuring sleeves are placed on the surface 
of the main chamber and both left and right latches are locked 
securely in place.  
Weekly Hood Cleaning and Initial Hood Cleaning  
Procedures:  
1. Weekly cleaning will be completed at the end of the shift on a 
designated day after all vials and supplies have been removed from 
the isolator.  
2. Prior to starting cleaning, perform hand hygiene and full garb (gown, 
mask, hair net, booties, and gloves).  
3. Sanitize gloved hands with a sterile 70% alcohol solution (IPA).  
4. Ensure the hood is off and open the front window of the hood by lifting 
the handles.  
5. Using disinfectant cleaner (see chart for approved disinfectants and dry 
times), first spray all hard surfaces ‚Äî do not spray ceiling or 
sleeves/gloves.  
6. Using low -particulate wipes, wipe each surface that was sprayed with 
disinfectant.  
7. Follow guidelines of working Top to Bottom and Back to Front. Use 
overlapping, linear strokes when cleaning.  
8. Ensure you use a new lint -free cloth for each chamber you clean. 
Change wipes if they become visibly soiled or begin shedding small 
particles.  
9. Surfaces to be cleaned:  
a. Back Wall (Main Chamber and Antechamber)  
b. Side Walls (Main Chamber and Antechamber)  
c. Work Surface (Main Chamber and Antechamber)  

DRIPBaR Franchising, LLC  
Confidential Franchise Operations Manual      Sanitizing and Maintenance  
Proprietary and Confidential Information   Page K -19 
Version Number: 1.0 January 2025  d. Area under Work Surface ‚Äî lift Work Surface tray (Main 
Chamber and Antechamber)  
e. Glove Port Window  
f. Transfer Door (both sides, Main Chamber and Antechamber)  
10. Following cleaning with disinfectant, repeat steps 1 -6 with the 
sporicidal agent (see the Hood Cleaning Protocol Chart for approved 
sporicidal agents and dry times).  
11. Following cleaning with the sporicidal agent, repeat steps 1 -6 with 
decontaminant (sterile 70% IPA) and lint -free cloths on all surfaces, 
including the sleeves/isolator gloves. Be sure to never  spray the ceiling 
of the isolator. Sterile IPA should always be the last step in the hood 
cleaning process and may be used on gloves and sleeves.  
12. Close the hood, carefully ensuring sleeves are placed on the surface 
of the main chamber and both left and right latches are locked 
securely in place.

The DRIPBaR Hood Cleaning Supplies List  
The DRIPBaR Hood Cleaning Supplies List aids in ordering and reordering 
supplies as needed. The products linked below are based on the lowest 
prices we found at the time; however, you may order other products from 
other vendors based on the approved cleani ng supplies list below.  
Please note you should always have 70% isopropyl alcohol, a disinfectant, 
sporicidal, and lab wipes on hand for hood cleaning.  
See The DRIPBaR Hood Cleaning Supplies List on the next page.
